## [LOCATIONS] Graf Granat's Domain
**Graf Granat's Domain** ｢グラナト伯 (はく) 爵 (しゃく) 領 (りょう) , *Guranato Hakushaku-ryō*?｣ is a fortified city and the surrounding region in the Northern Lands. It is a holding under the rule of the nobleman Graf Granat

## Overview]

Graf Granat's Domain consists of a fortified city and the land around it, ruled by the nobleman Graf Granat. A wall surrounds the settlement, with the Graf's mansion being centrally located. It has a dungeon to incarcerate offenders. The city features a church, many shops, houses, and inns, and is overall a prosperous town. It is protected by a defensive barrier, erected by the Great Mage Flamme a thousand years prior, that keeps monsters at bay.

### Terrain and Ecology]

The region around Graf Granat's Domain has mostly hilly terrain with snow-glazed mountains in the distance and a forest with majorly coniferous trees. In the town are domesticated animals, such as cats, and outside the barrier of the domain, there are dangerous creatures such as flying monsters and demons. Aura, one of the Seven Sages of Destruction and a demon at war against Graf Granat, devasted the surrounding forest with her undead army of withered soldiers and her henchman Lügner, Linie, and Draht.

### The Dungeon]

The dungeon is a brick-walled dungeon with several cells to incarcerate offenders. A guard is stationed outside the entrance. Each cell appears to have a flat bench and horizontal beams supporting the ceiling.

### The Graf's Mansion]

Graf Granat's mansion is a walled estate with a building several stories high. It features rooms of various sizes, such as a guest room with a balcony. In the house is also the room of Graf Granat's late son, which the Graf regularly cleans. He also displays a sword, granted to him after fighting in a duel, as the only thing that came back when his son died.

## Synopsis]

### History]

On the quest to defeat the Demon King, the Hero Party arrived near Graf Granat's Domain. They had a skirmish with Aura the Guillotine and wounded her, leaving her to flee and go into hiding.

After Himmel's death, Aura reappeared and waged war against Graf Granat, which led to the death of his son ten years prior to the arrival of Frieren's Party.

### Aura the Guillotine Arc]

Twenty-eight years after Himmel's passing, Frieren's Party enter the main town of Graf Granat's Domain. As the trio walks into town, Frieren senses some demons and tries to kill them, but she is stopped by guards. The three demons, led by Lügner, are supposedly peace envoys, but Frieren tells Lügner that he and the other demons are savage monsters that only mimic human speech. Frieren is thrown into the dungeon for attempting to attack the messengers, and Fern and Stark investigate the situation in the town, learning that Aura the Guillotine, a demon who served the Demon King as one of the Seven Sages of Destruction, has requested peace after being long at war with the town. They relay this information to Frieren, but Frieren states that it is futile to negotiate with the demons, as they only use words as a means of deception rather than communication. She decides to break out of the dungeon once the disorder starts. Meanwhile, Lügner wonders where he has seen Frieren before and smiles as she is the only one who knows the true nature of demons.

Graf Granat brings the demons into his late son's old room and tells them about him. He takes a sword on display, the only thing that came back after his son's death, and threatens the demons as vengeance for his son, declaring that he has no intention of reconciliation. However, Lügner claims that his father was also killed in the war, leading to Graf Granat emphasizing with him. Once the Graf leaves, Lügner explains to the one of the other envoys, the demon girl Linie, that his claim was actually a lie to placate the Graf. Meanwhile, the third envoy demon, Draht, goes to the dungeon to try to assassinate Frieren and decapitates a guard stationed outside in the process. He fails, and she is able to kill him easily. As Frieren exits the cell, she discovers the dead guard.

While Frieren is in the dungeon, Fern and Stark sit outside of a restaurant and plan their next actions, ultimately deciding that they will try and appeal to the Graf for Frieren's release. Back in the mansion's guest room, Lügner and Linie realizes Draht had been killed after being unable to detect his mana. They reconvene with the Graf and his guards, where Graf Granat discusses the escape of Frieren and the death of a guard. He then confronts Lügner, suspecting that Draht had beheaded the guard, as Frieren, who had allowed herself to be peacefully captured despite being a skilled mage, would understand the punishment associated with killing a guard. With his original plan now futile, Lügner reveals his true colors, killing the guards and wounding Graf Granat with his blood magic. Lügner tells the Graf his actual intention: removing the protective barrier surrounding the town.

As Fern and Stark head to the Graf's mansion, they notice a cloaked Frieren, who updates them and states that she will escape town to avoid punishment as the main suspect for the guard's death. Fern requests Frieren to not abandon the town, but Frieren tells her that the two of them are capable of dealing with Lügner and Linie. Frieren then sets her eye on Aura, who is at the outskirts the town with her undead army.

In the evening, Fern and Stark enter the Graf's mansion to kill the demons. Meanwhile, Lügner and Linie try to find a way to dispel the barrier through questioning the Graf, who is bound to a chair. Lügner gives him time to think, and he and Linie search for a grimoire that can dispel the barrier within the mansion. After the demons leave, Stark enters the room and tries to free the Graf. However, Lügner and Linie return from their search during the process, and Stark attempts to fight them. Lügner pins him down with his magic, but he does not detect Fern, who appears behind the window and blasts him with Zoltraak, severely wounding him. Given the severity of the Graf's wounds, Fern and Stark end up retreating. Linie attempts to pursue them, but Lügner advises her not to go alone, as he suspects that the magic that Fern used is from Frieren the Slayer, the mage that has led the most demons to their graves. In the meantime, Frieren arrives at the outskirts of the domain and confronts Aura and her army.

Fern, Stark, and the Graf make it to the town's church, where the Graf's wounds are treated. Fern and Stark go outside to evacuate the town and bring back Frieren, but Fern discovers mana on their blood-stained clothes on the way. They are promptly attacked by Lügner and Linie, and Linie knocks Stark off the building with an axe she conjured, leaving Fern to fight against Lügner and his blood magic, Balterie. Stark realizes Linie's magic, Erfassen, allows her to copy the movements of past warriors she had analyzed, including Eisen's, and he gets beaten down to the ground two times by her attacks. However, he realizes his master's technique dealt heavier blows than Linie's imitation, and he finishes her off with his **Lightning Strike** technique. With Lügner distracted by Linie's defeat, Fern is able to deal a deadly wound to him with Zoltraak. She casts the final blow to Lügner shortly after he notices that Fern and her master both suppress their mana.

As Fern and Stark battle against the envoys, Frieren face off against Aura outside of the town. Aura sends her army to attack Frieren, but she evades the attacks of the undead soldiers and releases some of them with dispelling magic, which removes the influence of Aura's Scales of Obedience. After a conversation with Frieren, Aura casts her Auserlese spell, which places her soul and Frieren's soul on the Scales of Obedience. Confident in her victory, Aura walks towards Frieren and takes up a sword from an undead soldier to personally behead the elf. However, the balance of the scales shifts, and Frieren reveals that she was suppressing her mana for over a thousand years, much longer than Aura's 500 years of life, and she releases her true mana. Having tipped the Scales in her favor, Frieren takes control of Aura. She commands the demon to kill herself, which she forcefully obeys by decapitating herself.

After the victory over Aura and her henchman, the town celebrates. Frieren, Fern, and Stark receive treatment for their wounds and help rebuild the damages. A commemoration is arranged, where Frieren receives a grimoire and Fern and Stark receive new winter outfits as gifts. At their farewell, the party discusses the next step: entering the Locations#Northern Plateau, which requires them to be accompanied by a first-class mage. Frieren and Fern thus decide to take the First-Class Mage Exam in Äußerst.

### First-Class Mage Exam Arc]

Around the same time Frieren, Fern and Stark reach the city of Äußerst, three months prior to the First-Class Mage Exam, Übel meets Kraft on the road by Graf Granat's Domain. After a brief interaction with Kraft, Übel continues traveling north to Äußerst.

## Inhabitants & Visitors]

## [LOCATIONS] Granz Channel
The **Granz Channel** ｢グランツ海 (かい) 峡 (きょう) , *Gurantsu Kaikyō*?｣ is a body of water in the Central Lands. Near the coast of the Granz Channel lies a small village, which Frieren and Fern visit.

## Overview]

The Granz Channel is used as a passageway for ships, and on the first sunrise of the new year, the Granz Channel becomes very picturesque because of the sunlight reflected on the untainted sea. Viewing this has been the tradition of the village situated near the cliffs on the coast of the Granz Channel.

### Terrain and Ecology]

The region around the Granz Channel has low vegetation with some sparse trees spread in the area, and the channel itself has a beach rim in. The villagers grow greenery and colorful flowers in flower pots and planters. Aquatic species, such as seaweed and other water plants, are part of the ecosystem, feeding fish and other creatures like starfish. 

### The Village]

On the cliffs overlooking the coast of the Granz Channel lies a small village. The village has plenty of houses, shops, inns, and a church.

The village has a tradition of watching the New Year's sunrise because of how picturesque the Granz Channel looks. The coast was initially littered with shipwrecks that washed up on shore until Frieren and Fern were hired to clean the coast up. As payment, they received the only grimoire in the village, which was supposedly from the Great Mage Flamme.

## Synopsis]

### History]

During the time of the Hero Party's journey, the party stopped in the Granz Channel during the New Year's festival. At the time, the coastline was free of debris. Himmel wanted the party to watch the sunrise together, but Frieren slept in instead, as she didn't see the value of getting up early just to see a sunrise. 

This would later cause Himmel to gently rebuke her by stating that Heiter was so disappointed that his condition had deteriorated from the sadness, though in reality, it was the result of a hangover. Frieren interjects that she doesn't see what the big deal is, since the rest of the party was able to see the sunrise and she personally did not think it would have been fun. However, Himmel tells Frieren that the party had wanted her to enjoy the sunrise as well, and that she would have had fun because that is who she is.

### Beyond Journey's End Arc]

Frieren and Fern are hired to clean the coast of the village next to the Granz Channel, with a supposed grimoire from the Great Mage Flamme as a reward. They commence cleaning operations and, after clearing the coast for over three months, finish just in time for the New Year's sunrise.

Frieren is awoken by Fern to see the sunrise, and she thinks back to when she and the Hero Party were there and did not participate in the sunrise viewing. Decades later, with Fern, she now understands the beauty in viewing the sight with others.

## Inhabitants & Visitors]

### Inhabitants]

- Granz Channel village chief

- Granz Channel bakery owner

### Visitors]

- Frieren

- Fern

- Himmel

- Heiter

- Eisen

## Events]

- Frieren and Fern clean up the Granz Channel and the village beach.

- Frieren and Fern spend New Year's in the channel and attend the the New Year's Festival sunrise viewing together.

## [LOCATIONS] Great Sanft Forest
The **Great Sanft Forest** ｢ザンフト大 (だい) 森 (しん) 林 (りん) , *Zanfuto Daishinrin*?｣ is a heavily forested region located in the Northern Lands.

## Overview]

The Great Sanft Forest is situated in the Northern Lands. A small river runs through this heavily forested region with deciduous trees. The region's main road splits at a fork, with one branch leading to Neutral Harbor and the other to the Northern Plateau. A small settlement lies at this junction, with an inn where adventurers can rest. The inn’s hanging sign bears the letters “WG.”

## Synopsis]

### Continued Northern Travels Arc]

Twenty-nine years after the death of Himmel the Hero, Stark returns to the campsite of Frieren's Party, hoping his foraged food is enough for lunch. However, he finds that both Fern and Frieren are missing, so he decides to catch some big fish. Meanwhile, Fern and Frieren are bathing and cleaning their belongings in a river. Stark eventually finds them there while on his way to fish.

Shortly thereafter, the group continues their journey and arrives at a fork where one path leads to Neutral Harbor and the other to the Northern Plateau. Nearby, they find an inn where they decide to rest. While there, they reunite with Wirbel, Ehre, and Scharf. After a brief exchange, Wirbel asks Frieren if he can try to convince Stark to temporarily join them in their fight against demons on the Northern Frontier. Although Fern is reluctant, Frieren agrees to let Wirbel proceed.

Later, Fern talks with Stark, who reveals that he turned down Wirbel's request. He confesses that when Fern and Frieren first met him near Riegel Canyon, he was at his breaking point and considered abandoning the village. He shares that Fern’s encouragement that night motivated him to stay and asks her to be nicer to him.

The next day, Frieren and her party bid farewell to Wirbel and his group as both continue on their respective journeys—Wirbel and his team heading to Neutral Harbor to reach the Imperial Capital, while Frieren and her party continue on their way to the Northern Plateau.

## Inhabitants & Visitors]

### Visitors]

- Frieren

- Fern

- Stark

- Wirbel

- Ehre

- Scharf

## Events]

- Frieren's Party meets up with Wirbel, Ehre, and Scharf again.

## Gallery]

### Anime]

The Great Sanft Forest.The inn located by a fork in the Great Sanft Forest.

### Manga]

The Great Sanft Forest.The fork in the road in the Great Sanft Forest.

## Trivia]

- "Sanft" in German means "gentle" or "soft".

- "Weiche" in German as a noun in the context of railway means switch, and in the context of animals it is the side as a body part, but when used as an adjective it describes the property of "softness".

- "WG" in German is an acronym for the word "Wohnungsgemeinschaft" and describes a community of people (roommates) who share an apartment.

## [LOCATIONS] Great Tor Canyon
The **Great Tor Canyon** ｢トーア大 (だい) 渓 (けい) 谷 (こく) , *Tōa Daikeikoku*?｣ is a vast canyon located in the Northern Plateau. It is said to be the deepest canyon on the continent.

## Overview]

The Great Tor Canyon is the deepest canyon on the continent, with a precipice reaching 3000 meters. From the top, the canyon's floor is barely visible. Its existence is made possible by the high elevation of the Northern Plateau. Due to the strong winds that sweep through the canyon, crossing it with flying magic is impossible.

One specific detour around the Great Tor Canyon requires crossing a river on the upper reaches, and navigating a steep mountain range. Further downriver, the canyon ends in a sheer cliff, 3000 meters high, that drops into the ocean. Circumventing the entire canyon would take roughly two weeks. 

Due to a newly constructed bridge that spans the canyon upriver, both sides are now connected, facilitating easier travel across the canyon.

To the south of the Great Tor Canyon lies Lake Korridor, while the Schmal Snowfield and the Weise Region are situated to the north. Additionally, a city with a garrison is located nearby to provide defense. On the opposite side of the canyon from this city lies Gehen's village.

## Synopsis]

### History]

During their quest to subjugate the Demon King, the Hero Party arrived at the Great Tor Canyon and discovered that Gehen's bridge was still under construction. Due to Gehen's lack of funds, Himmel offered him the monetary reward they had received from Graf Dach for retrieving his heirloom sword. Although Gehen initially hesitated, stating that he could not accept the reward because Himmel would likely be long dead by the time the bridge was completed, Himmel insisted that Frieren could take the reward on his behalf. He instructed Gehen to ensure that the bridge was built to last a thousand years, to which Gehen readily agreed.

### The Golden Land Arc]

Thirty years after the death of Himmel the Hero, Frieren and her party arrive at the Great Tor Canyon. Remembering Gehen's bridge, Frieren takes Fern and Stark upriver to check on its status. There, Gehen informs her that bird monsters have been attacking anyone who attempts to cross the bridge. In exchange for a spell that lets you flip pancakes perfectly, Frieren's party agrees to exterminate the bird monster nest and succeed, ensuring that everyone can safely cross the Great Tor Canyon.

## Inhabitants & Visitors]

### Inhabitants]

- Gehen

### Visitors]

- Frieren

- Himmel

- Eisen

- Heiter

- Fern

- Stark

## Events]

- Frieren's Party clears out a nest of bird monsters to ensure safe passage over the Great Tor Canyon's bridge.

## Gallery]

### Manga]

Great Tor Canyon.Gehen's bridge over the canyon.

## Trivia]

- "Tor" is German for "gate" or "door", referring to an entrance or opening that allows passage between two areas.

## [LOCATIONS] Grobe Basin
The **Grobe Basin** ｢グローブ盆 (ぼん) 地 (ち) , *Gurōbu Bonchi*?｣ is a forested basin situated in the Kühl Region in the Northern Lands. Its lake and the area around it serves as the test location for the first stage of the First-Class Mage Exam in Äußerst, proctored by Genau. A barrier was placed over a large portion of the basin for the exam.

## Overview]

### Terrain and Ecology]

The Grobe Basin is located within the Kühl Region in the Northern Lands. It sits on a lower plane surrounded by hills with caves and mountains, and creeks and rivers flow into a central lake. The area is densely forested with deciduous trees and much undergrowth. The basin features rich wildlife, including beasts and meteoric iron birds, Stilles. Dangerous creatures are also present, such as the Geisel.

## Synopsis]

### First-Class Mage Exam (First Stage)]

*Main article: First-Class Mage Exam*

Twenty-nine years after Hero Himmel's passing, 57 examinees of the First-Class Mage Exam, including Frieren and Fern, are divided into groups of three for the first stage of the exam. In Frieren's group, titled the second party, are Kanne and Lawine, while Fern's group, the fourth party, consists of her, Übel, and Land. Genau, the first-class mage proctoring the test, chooses the Grobe Basin as the location for the first stage. He announces that the goal of the exam is to capture a Stille—a meteoric iron bird that can fly faster than the speed of sound—in a cage by sunset the next day, with the caveat that all party members must be present. Because the Stille is sensitive to mana and the birds' own mana is difficult to detect, many participants are forced into battles with each other in order to try to secure a bird. Additionally, the participants need to take into account the geographical features of the basin,, including the barrier placed by Serie that prevents rain and river water from entering the basin, as well as the ecology of the basin, especially the Geisel aerial monsters.

Because the young mages in Frieren's group bicker, she is forced to take the lead. They introduce themselves to each other, and Frieren says she has some knowledge of the Stille but has never seen one herself. The group investigates the area for signs of a Stille. When they take a break, Lawine declares herself stronger than Kanne and goes scouting ahead to find a Stille. Frieren tells Lawine to be careful of the sky, which confuses Kanne. Lawine manages to find a Stille and leads Kanne and Frieren to a small body of water. Kanne uses her water magic to surround the bird, and Lawine promptly freezes the water with her magic to immobilize a Stille. They trap the Stille in ice, but it breaks free and speeds away with its supersonic speed. Frieren takes note of Kanne and Lawine's strong teamwork, and the group spends the rest of the day observing the habits of the bird.

Late at night, Kanne wakes up at the camp and notices Frieren is gone. As she searches for her, a Geisel attacks her and knocks away her staff. Suddenly, Frieren rescues her while also trying out her folk-magic spell to capture a bird. Kanne calms down after the surprise attack and walks back to the camp with Frieren, where they have a conversation about how Kanne looks back fondly towards Lawine's efforts to help her improve. Around the same time, Fern manages to catch a Stille and returns to her group members.

The next day, Frieren's group strategizes about how to catch a Stille with the information they gathered. Frieren proposes the idea of infuse bodies of water with mana, which should drive the thirsty Stille to a body of water without mana. Meanwhile, Fern's group searches for water after capturing their Stille. On their way, they are ambushed by the eighth party, consisting of Wirbel, Ehre, and Scharf. The groups prepare to face off in pairs, but they're suddenly interrupted by a large release of mana, caused by Lawine freezing the central lake over as part of Frieren's strategy.

Fern is matched up against Ehre, who uses her Doragate spell to change rocks into bullets, bombarding Fern with the projectiles. Ehre remarks that fighting against Fern's technique feels like fighting against her grandfather, and she notes how Fern only uses ordinary offensive and defensive magic. Fern sees Fern sees Ehre as the strongest of her group, while Ehre thinks Wirbel is. They engage in an exchange of attacks. Fern uses a barrage of offensive magic, which presses down Ehre's defense and ultimately defeats her. 

At the same time, Scharf and Land stand off at a clearing. Scharf uses his magic, Jubelade, to turn flower petals into metal, precisely slicing Land and rendering his right arm unusable. However, Land tells Scharf that he should be more observant of his opponents and that he is lacking in the fundamentals, such as mana detection. Scharf ignores his words and attacks, but Land appears behind him to take him out of action with a shock spell. Land reveals that Scharf did not fight him, but rather his clone.

Übel attacks Wirbel with her Reelseiden spell, which can slash through almost anything. Wirbel learns that the spell is short-ranged and exploits an opening to use his binding spell: Sorganeil, and he declares he can easily kill her now. With Übel restrained, he gives her the chance to walk off and leave the cage with the Stille behind. Übel concludes that the binding spell has a condition that requires the opponent be in full view for it to work. She throws the cage as a distraction into the air, making Wirbel look up and forcing him to release Sorganeil. Übel takes this opportunity to charge Wirbel, narrowly missing a slash to his eyes. He binds her again, and they have a conversation about how there are people who enjoy killing. Übel's personal belief is that the magic someone specializes in is connected to their life and character. She deduces Wirbel's binding spell gives him time to prepare to kill somebody, to which Wirbel agrees. As he charges a spell to kill Übel, Fern appears besides him and prompts him to stop. 

Wirbel asks if Fern killed Ehre, and she confirms that she did. He concludes that by losing one of their party members, his party has lost. Wirbel walks away and releases Übel from the binding. After Fern and Übel leave, he searches for Ehre and finds her out of mana at the location where she fought Fern. As Wirbel carries her on his back to find Scharf, they come across him incapacitated from Land's blow. Wirbel floats the mage with a spell and the three move on searching for a Stille. During a conversation about Wirbel's intention to become a first-class mage, the group manages to find and catch a Stille, which they hold on to until the end of the exam.

While the fourth and eighth parties fight, others try to melt the ice. Some groups around the lake reorientate their efforts to finding and catching a Stille in other places, as the lake with mana infusion would repel the birds. Denken, a member of the thirteenth party with Richter and Laufen, notices that Frieren's group must have a plan and proposes to take away their Stille. As Denken's group waits for Frieren to catch the bird, they come across another group that has fallen victim to the Geisel. When Laufen suggests taking the bodies out of the trees, Denken explains the monster's hunting trick: they lure prey with the corpses of their victims. The group then continues to lay in wait for Frieren's next move.

In the meantime, Frieren and Kanne infuse bodies of water with faint traces of mana to deter the Stille. They come together at a waterhole without mana infusion. Frieren suppresses her mana to a minimum while the other two members of her party hide nearby. As Frieren waits for a Stille, multiple beasts and monsters, including the Geisel, drink from the waterhole without paying attention to Frieren's presence. A Stille eventually lands on Frieren's shoulder, and she captures it with her folk magic. However, she releases mana in the process, which alerts Denken's team to her location. Laufen uses her high speed movement spell: Jilwer to close the distance and take away the cage with the Stille. Denken and Richter reveal themselves and prepare for battle, as the inexperienced Laufen has left mana traces that Frieren could follow to take the Stille back. 

Denken recognizes Frieren as the mage of the Hero Party. Frieren has noticed that her group was followed and is surprised that Denken challenges her. At first, Richter wants to kill Frieren's other two group members and secure the privilege granted by Serie, but Denken tells him to just hold them back. Richter begrudgingly complies and separates the two groups with his earth control spell: Bargland, raising himself, Kanne, and Lawine out of the ground and onto a mesa-like platform. As they prepare to fight, Denken tells Frieren that his reason for fighting isn't the privilege, but rather, the joy that comes with the pursuit of magic itself. Denken's words remind Frieren of her first meeting with Serie, and she vocalizes her agreement with Denken's perspective.

While Denken and Frieren fight, Richter shuts down Kanne and Lawine's attempts at defeating him, criticizing Lawine's freezing techniques that lack strength and Kanne's reliance on existing water. He gives them a lesson about the latest developments of magic used to fight, declaring that his earth manipulation, which makes use of overwhelming mass, can easily overcome the two mages' defenses. After Richter overpowers them, the three stop fighting as they wait for the conclusion of the fight between Frieren and Denken.

Frieren and Denken fight in the air until Denken realizes that he cannot sustain his defenses with his depleting mana. Denken lands and creates a fire tornado combining Waldgose, his tornado wind spell and Daosdorg, his wind-to-hellfire spell to attack Frieren, but she effortlessly resists with a sphere of defensive magic. Denken attempts to whittle Frieren with his Lights of Judgment spell: Catastravia down, but she unleashes a counterattack and closes the distance to blast him with offensive magic, exhausting his mana. First-class mages Genau and Sense witness their battle from afar, and Sense questions the strength of the barrier. She also reveals that someone had been analyzing the barrier, but Genau disregards her worries, as the barrier was enacted by Serie.

To get back the Stille, Frieren prompts Laufen to rescue Denken by acting like she would harm him. Laufen uses Jilwer to get Denken out of harm's way but is caught by Frieren. She then takes back the Stille and binds Laufen and Denken to a tree with magic. With the defeat of Denken, Richter takes action to kill Frieren's group members. However, Frieren finishes her analysis of the barrier and casts a spell to dispel it, which catches Serie's attention. Rain starts pouring inside the testing ground, and Kanne is free to manipulate the water. She casts her water manipulation magic, Reamstroha, which creates a giant sphere of water that she drops on Richter. The mass of her attack crushes Richter's defenses, and he is washed off the mesa. Frieren regroups with her teammates and congratulates them on defeating Richter. They continue defending their Stille until the end of the exam. Genau and Sense watch the barrier shatter, and Genau demands to know who Frieren is. Sense informs him that she is Frieren, the mage of the Hero Party and a holder of a Holy Emblem, signifying the elf's Great Mage status.

Richter is washed to Denken and Laufen, and Laufen frees herself and Denken from their restraints by cutting the tree they are tied to. Despite Denken and Richter being completely out of mana, Denken refuses to give up and suggests they search for other teams that are in similar situations. They come across a party that has lost a member, disqualifying them, but they still defend their Stille. Denken and Richter secure the bird with a fistfight and are able to keel it until the end of the exam. Meanwhile, Fern's group takes shelter from the rain in a cave. Fern and Übel talk about spells, and Land urges Fern not to give away all her abilities since they could end up as enemies at a later stage. They stay until the evening and pass the exam.

In the evening, Genau declares the exam is over. Out of the original 57 examinees, 18 manage to pass the first stage of the exam.

## Trivia]

- The Grobe Basin was localized as the "Größe Basin" by Viz Media, where "Größe" would be German for "size / extent / bigness," the same as the Größe Forest. However, official media for the anime call the basin the "Grobe Basin." The German term "grob" would mean "rough / rude / tough."

## [ARCS] Episode 1
**The Journey's End** ｢冒 (ぼう) 険 (けん) の終 (お) わり, *Bōken no owari*?｣ is the first episode of the *Frieren: Beyond Journey's End* anime series. It is the first part of the initial two-hour premier episode, released on September 29, 2023.

## Synopsis]

The world celebrates the Demon King's defeat at the hands of the Hero and his companions. Now that their great adventure is over, what will Frieren the mage do next? 

## Plot]

The Hero Party, consisting of Frieren the Mage and her companions Himmel the Hero, Heiter the Priest, and Eisen the Warrior. They return to the Royal Capital after triumphantly defeating the Demon King. On their way, Himmel suggests that despite their achievements, they still need to seek employment upon their arrival and continue forward with their lives. He tells Frieren that the life ahead of her will be much longer than theirs, which she nonchalantly agrees with. The heroes reach the city amidst a large celebration in their honor and receive recognition from the King.

That night, they enjoy a festival held by the townsfolk, during which Himmel informs the others that the King intends to erect statues of them in the plaza. The Hero Party reminisce on their journey and the humorous moments that had occurred throughout it, finding it hard to believe that it has come to an end after ten years. Himmel expresses his gratitude towards his companions for the time he spent and the memories he made on the journey with them. Frieren points out that they spent a mere ten years together, surprising Himmel. They all look up into the sky to witness the Era Meteors, an event that occurs only once every fifty years, and Himmel decides to label it as the start of an era of peace. Frieren proposes that she brings the party to a better location for viewing the meteors the next time they occur, and Himmel laughs and accepts the offer.

The next day, Himmel and the others accompany Frieren to a bridge to bid her farewell. She informs them that she plans on traveling through the Central Lands for the next century and collect spells, though she may visit them every now and then. As she departs, Himmel wonders about the life she will lead, and Heiter refers to how time passes differently for her.

Frieren immerses in various experiences and activities during her solo journey for the next fifty years. She visits a shop in an attempt to obtain a Shadow Dragon's Horn, but the shop owner informs her that the shop does not have one. Frieren remembers that the Hero Party found a horn during their exploration of the Demon King's castle and she had left it with Himmel for safekeeping. With the next occurrence of the Era Meteors approaching, Frieren decides to head back to the Royal Capital and retrieve it from him upon their reunion.

Upon returning to the city, Frieren is shocked by how much it has changed. When Himmel reunites with her, she is equally surprised by how much he has aged. Himmel reminds the elf Frieren that fifty years have passed, though he remarks that she still looks the same. He presents the shadow dragon's horn to Frieren, stating that he had always intended to return it to her someday. She and Himmel then prepare for the upcoming Era Meteors at Himmel's home.

The two reunite with Heiter, who is now a bishop in the Holy City, and Eisen, and Frieren notices that while Heiter has also aged considerably, Eisen's appearance remains relatively unchanged due to his longer dwarven lifespan. Frieren informs them that it will take a week to reach the location with a better view of the Era Meteors, which disappoints Himmel. As they adventure to the location, Himmel reflects on their memories and how much he had missed traveling with his comrades. The reunited party arrives at a giant lake underneath a clear sky, and as they once again watch the Era Meteors, Himmel expresses gratitude to Frieren for providing him with a wonderful final adventure.

Shortly after, Himmel passes away, and the remaining members of the Hero Party attend his funeral. As the bishop, Heiter holds his funeral. In his coffin, Himmel is surrounded by flowers and dressed in his hero's attire with his sword. During the procession, Heiter mentions to Frieren and Eisen that Himmel was happy. Numerous civilians gather to pay their respects, and Frieren overhears people gossiping about her apparent lack of emotion at the passing of one of her companions. Heiter defends Frieren, reminding them that he and Eisen were also Himmel's allies and yet, they are not expressing sadness. As Himmel is buried, Frieren reminisces about the time she spent with him. Despite only traveling with him, merely for ten years, Frieren begins to cry, regretting not getting to know Himmel better. Heiter and Eisen offer her comfort.

After the funeral, Frieren and Eisen bid farewell to Heiter, who is returning to the Holy City. Before leaving, Heiter jokes about the possibility of this event being the last time he will see them, prompting Frieren to question if he is unafraid of passing away. Heiter reminds Frieren that they are legendary heroes and believes they will lead a good life in Heaven after death. After Heiter departs, Frieren confides in Eisen that she plans to learn more about humans and asks if he can accompany her. He reminds her that he is too old and his age will be a hindrance in combat, however, he reassures her that his life has slowed down past his prime. They bid farewell to each other and go their separate ways.

Twenty years after Himmel's death, Frieren finds herself lost in the woods at the outskirts of the Holy City in the Central Lands. A young girl discovers Frieren and guides her to Heiter's residence, where Frieren is astonished to discover that Heiter is still alive. Heiter introduces the girl as Fern and reveals that she is a war orphan from the Southern Lands. Frieren explains that she had been traveling the continent to learn about humans but stopped by to repay her debt to Heiter before his death. Heiter asks if Frieren could mentor Fern as an apprentice given that Fern shows potential as a mage, but Frieren declines, fearing that Fern's inexperience would hinder her. Additionally, she points out that apprentice mages frequently die in battle, and she cannot allow for that to happen to Fern.

Heiter acknowledges Frieren's decision and asks if she can instead decipher a grimoire depicting immortality and resurrection that was written by Ewig the Sage. Frieren accepts his request and tells him she can finish deciphering the grimoire in five to six years, though she wonders why he is interested in the topic despite having been unafraid of death twenty years ago. He jokingly tells her that the holy texts say to live healthy lives, and he now admits that he now fears death the more he approaches it and simply wishes for more time. He asks Frieren to teach Fern magic in her spare time, and Frieren concedes.

Frieren goes to look for Fern and finds her by a cliff overlooking a ravine. She tells the young girl that she had trouble looking for her, but Fern points out that being difficult to find is a good thing. Frieren agrees and wonders to herself how Fern had established a high level of mana control at such a young age. Fern informs Frieren that Heiter mentioned she would be close to becoming a proper mage when she could blast a large rock at the opposite end of the ravine. As Frieren endorses the method, Fern immediately casts a beam of offensive magic that nearly hits the rock. She explains to Frieren that her magic dissipates before making contact and asks how she should train it. Before Frieren gives her advice, she asks if Fern enjoys magic, and Fern admits that she somewhat likes it. Frieren notes they are alike in that sense.

## Episode Notes]

- The world map of the continent shown at the start with a quote by the legendary mage Flamme is not depicted in Chapter 1 of the manga.

- The Hero Party passing through the entrance of the Royal Capital and receiving a triumphant reception is anime original. In the manga, the Hero Party directly goes to the King.

- In the manga, Himmel and Eisen are shown locked in a guillotine for being rude to the King. In the anime, they are about to be executed with a sword instead.

- The scene where Frieren lays in a river in the time montage is anime original.

- A panel where two ladies are seen gossiping and questioning why Frieren does not show a hint of sorrow is depicted in the manga, but in the anime, they are only voiced.

- When Frieren grieves and cries over Himmel's death, it takes place inside the church in the manga, compared to outside at the burial of Himmel's coffin in the anime.

- The dead tree that Frieren uses as a navigation reference when searching for Heiter's house is not prominent in the manga.

## [ARCS] Episode 2
**It Didn't Have to Be Magic...** ｢別 (べつ) に魔 (ま) 法 (ほう) じゃなくたって…, *Betsu ni mahō ja nakutatte…*?｣ is the second episode of the *Frieren: Beyond Journey's End* anime series. It is the second part of the initial two-hour premier episode, released on September 29, 2023.

## Synopsis]

Frieren instructs Fern in the use of magic while deciphering a grimoire for Heiter. 

## Plot]

Frieren begins to teach Fern the basics of long-range magic, emphasizing that Fern's mana output and strength will require years of training to master. However, her control over mana, an aspect many mages struggle with, is very high. Over the next four years, Frieren continues to decipher the grimoire while Fern diligently trains under the elf's tutelage and alone in the woods.

When asked about the child's progress by Heiter, Frieren explains that she has learned more than most people would in a decade and that she is studying a little too hard. Suddenly, Heiter collapses, and he later becomes bedridden. Heiter remarks that it is miracle that he had been mobile for so long and Frieren ensures him that she will decipher the grimoire quickly. The elf then tells Fern to pause her training on the cliff to stay by Heiter's side, but Fern rejects this notion, saying that she has to be able to hit the rock with her magic before the priest's death.

A backstory shows that a younger Fern, who had lost her parents and home, was about to jump off a cliff in the aftermath of a war before being stopped by an aged Heiter, who says that it would be a waste for her to die. He explains that he once lost an old friend of his who never abandoned anyone who was in need, supposing that if he were to stay alive, more people would've been saved by his hands compared to the priest's. Heiter had planned to lived his life quietly, but came to the realization that everything that he learned, including precious memories, from his friend would go to waste that way. Likewise for Fern, he believes that the child holds precious memories that should not go wasted.

Having been saved by Heiter, Fern believes that the best way to repay him is to learn any skill that would help her survive so that he could remain glad that she was saved and will manage to be safe on her own. Convinced by the child's convictions, Frieren allows her to continue training as she continues to decipher the grimoire that could possibly save Heiter.

Eventually, Fern is finally able to achieve her goal of hitting the rock with her offensive magic spell while Frieren finishes deciphering the grimoire, which she concludes does not contain any spells related to revival or immortality. This revelation, however, does not surprise Heiter, who supposes that Ewig the Sage would have used the spell himself if it was true. With Frieren's approval of Fern being a proper mage, Heiter reveals that his main objective all along was to have Fern learn enough that she would not be a hindrance to Frieren as the elf's traveling apprentice. 

Heiter requests that the two leave the same night before his death so that Fern does not lose anyone anymore, but an emotional Frieren rejects this and tells Heiter to give the child a proper farewell and to make as many memories as possible. When asked why he saved Fern, Heiter gives the reasoning that Himmel the Hero would have done the same thing. Later, Frieren climbs the same cliff where she met Fern to witness the fruits of the child's training. 

 
Heiter's death eventually arrives as Fern expresses gratitude to Frieren for allowing her to repay the priest as the elf pours two full bottles of alcohol over his tombstone. The two depart from Strahl and finally set off on their journey.

Over the next few years, Frieren and Fern perform odd and simple jobs in exchange for magic spells. They eventually arrive at the Turk Region. The duo use their magic to harvest pumpkins. The payment for helping to harvest was given by the pumpkin farmer in the form of a spell that makes hot tea. Fern does not see the appeal in collecting spells for removing rust of bronze statue or a spell turning sweet grapes sour. Fern believes that the two share slightly different views on magic, but Frieren insists that they are both the same in loving magic. Later on, they come upon a herbalist who requests the two for help in cleaning the statue of Himmel, who had saved her life in the past, in exchange for information about the local flora. The statue is then cleaned by them, however, not before Frieren reminisces about how long it took for the hero to settle on a pose for the statue.

The herbalist plans to add some flowers to give the statue more color, but before Frieren casts a flower bed-making spell, she remembers that Himmel used to love blue-moon weed flowers, though she has never seen them herself. The herbalist claims that it has been decades since the flowers have been spotted, but this does not stop Frieren from searching for them. Before leaving, Frieren spots Fern hiding seed rats in her robe as the latter claims that she will release them in the forest.

Six months pass into Frieren's search for the flowers, and Fern is discouraged to learn that the elf does not plan on stopping anytime soon. An impatient Fern vents to the herbalist about how Frieren should not be spending her time searching for something that doesn't exist. In response to this, the herbalist hands Fern a bag of seeds of a related species and tells Fern to convey her feelings to the elf as she must see things very differently to humans.

As Fern expresses her feelings to Frieren, the latter understands that she is no longer on her own time and claims that the search will end soon. Fern is displeased to hear "soon", but before she can continue the conversation, the two spot a seed rat that takes the bag of seeds and they proceed to follow it. Fern asks Frieren why she collects spells, and although it may seem more than that, Frieren insists that it was just a hobby that an idiot complimented. Frieren has a flashback to said idiot where she used the spell to produce a field of flowers. All members of the Hero Party enjoyed the moment.

The two eventually spot a tower the seed rat wandered to. Frieren lectures her apprentice that seed rats would bury and often forget about things they collect. Frieren flies towards the top of the tower as a flashback occurs in which the previous is continued and Himmel is seen wishing to view the blue-moon weed flowers with Frieren. The top of the tower is revealed to be full of said flowers as Fern soon follows Frieren from behind. Fern continues to not understand why Frieren loves magic, but the latter insists that she does understand as she chose to learn magic above all else.

Himmel's statue is finally decorated with a bed of blue-moon weed flowers to the satisfaction of the herbalist. Before Frieren and Fern leave, Frieren place a wreath of flowers on top of Himmel's head as she remembers the wreaths on her comrade's heads.

## Episode Notes]

- In the manga, the three essential elements of long-range magic are not specified. The scene where Frieren explains these elements to Fern is original to the anime.

- The anime makes it appear that Fern is in the kitchen preparing food as she listens to the conversation between Heiter and Frieren about Heiter's imminent death. In the manga, the conversation occurs in Heiter's room, but Fern is not shown to explicitly overhear it.

- Frieren's search for a spell that produces hot tea allegedly stems from Himmel questioning her if such a spell existed, which is mentioned in the spin-off *Frieren Makes a Detour*.

- The scene of Himmel looking at the young herbalist while placing his sword in its scabbard after defeating the monster is anime original.

- The home of the herbalist is located in the middle of the village in the manga, whereas in the anime, it is located within a remote area in the woods.

- While Frieren talks to Fern about searching for the blue-moon weed, she stares at a leaf and twirls it in her hand in the anime. In the manga, a visual of a blue-moon weed flower is used instead.

- The anime includes an additional scene of Frieren and Fern sunbathing during the time they spend searching for the blue-moon weed.

- Frieren uses her spell to make a field of flowers for the Hero Party in a flashback, but instead of casting it in an open space like she does in the manga, the anime shows her casting it outside the ruins of a church with a statue of the Goddess of Creation.

## [ARCS] Episode 3
**Killing Magic** ｢人 (ひと) を殺 (ころ) す魔 (ま) 法 (ほう) , *Hito o korosu mahō*?｣ is the third episode of the *Frieren: Beyond Journey's End* anime series. It is the third part of the initial two-hour premier episode, released on September 29, 2023.

## Synopsis]

While retracing the path she took on her adventure with her former traveling companions, Frieren confronts an old enemy. 

## Plot]

Twenty-seven years after Himmel the Hero's passing, Frieren and Fern find themselves in the trade city of Warm in the Central Lands. As they stroll through the city, Frieren instructs Fern to split up and restock their travel supplies. Fern, realizing most responsibilities fall on her, asks about Frieren's shopping plans. Frieren pauses before responding that she plans on buying herbs and the likes. Reading Frieren's suspicious expression, Fern recalls instances when Frieren purchased a monster's skull, a cloth-dissolving potion that she was told to return, and a book on magical history. Fern hesitates to deem the last item unnecessary.

As Frieren takes a different path at a fork, Fern decides to tail her, mindful of their travel expenses. Observing Frieren at an accessory shop, Fern speculates that, despite her usual neglect of hair care, Frieren might have an interest in fashion. Fern looks at an incredibly perplexed Frieren from behind as she remarks that her master has never made such a face before. After a long time which Fern spent petting a cat, Frieren finally buys an accessory and Fern supposes that one accessory would not be too bad.

As Fern decides to start shopping, she overhears Frieren asking about good desserts in town, which Fern finds unfair, given her own sweets deprivation for months. Frieren is directed to a dubious tavern, where she inquires about desserts, garnering responses from intimidating, but passionate adventurers. As Frieren bids farewell, Fern realizes she's heading back to the inn rather than a dessert shop, and that Fern has not done any shopping yet. 

Later at the inn, Frieren tells Fern she's late, and Fern apologizes. As Fern sets down her purchased items, Frieren suggests getting something sweet to eat and awkwardly exits the room.

Frieren and Fern arrive at the recommended place, and Frieren admires the view of the sun and the city, appreciating the adventurers' suggestion. Fern then apologizes to Frieren for doubting her, although Frieren has no idea what she is talking about. Frieren encourages Fern to choose whatever she likes and reveals her secret savings to cover the expenses. When Frieren wonders what she herself will have, Fern surprises her by correctly guessing that she feels like eating Merkur pudding.

In a flashback, the Hero Party dined together, and Himmel accurately guessed that Frieren desired Merkur pudding. Curious, Frieren questioned how he knew, and Himmel attributed it to years of traveling together. Frieren admitted knowing nothing about the rest of the party, prompting Himmel to promise to share more about himself. He revealed his favorite meal was a Ruf-omelette, while Eisen mentioned his preference for sour grapes. Before Heiter could share his choice, Frieren interjected, stating she already knew he liked alcohol. Eisen tells Heiter not to blush, and Himmel noted it was concerning that Frieren only remembered that detail.

The flashback ends, and Frieren apologizes to Fern for not knowing her preferences. Frieren then presents Fern with a box, and Fern realizes it's her birthday. Opening the box, she finds a beautifully crafted hair ornament with a butterfly motif. Grateful, Fern thanks Frieren, appreciating the thoughtful gift. Despite Frieren's apparent cluelessness, Fern affectionately remarks on Frieren's attempts to understand her, finding joy in the effort, even if Frieren doesn't fully grasp human emotions.

The following morning, Frieren and Fern resume their journey, with Fern proudly wearing her new hair ornament. As they walk along a road, Fern questions the purpose of their journey. Frieren responds that it's primarily to fulfill her desire to collect spells, although she also expresses a desire to retrace the adventure she had with Himmel and the Hero Party before the signs of their existence vanish. Fern acknowledges the importance of this to Frieren, but Frieren admits she's not entirely sure and intends to discover more about it as they progress.

As the two walk, Frieren observes that Fern has grown taller again. Fern mentions that she is now sixteen, old enough to be an older sister. Frieren glances at Fern’s chest and notes that it's strange Fern has developed more despite sharing the same diet.

Later, Frieren and Fern are training in the Größe Forest. Frieren casts a spell at Fern, who promptly blocks it with a defensive spell which shields her front. Frieren notes Fern's improvement but challenges her further with a spell that bends through her defenses and dissipates before hitting Fern. In surprise, the young mage drops to her knees. Frieren emphasizes the importance of addressing defensive gaps in a real battle. The training intensifies as Frieren launches multiple spells, prompting Fern to correctly respond with an omnidirectional-shielding spherical defensive spell as Frieren continues with more spells. Fern becomes fatigued, leading Frieren to conclude the training.

As they walk, Frieren explains to Fern that the defensive spell is powerful but depletes mana rapidly. Expanding it continuously would exhaust one's mana supply within seconds. Fern deduces that casting smaller spells at the moment of impact for each spell is a more efficient strategy, and Frieren confirms. Fern notes that they have only been training in defensive magic and Frieren replies it is because it is directly linked to their survival. Fern agrees, noting how strange it is how powerful the defensive spells are. 

Frieren tugs Fern’s arm as she realizes that Fern has not read the magical history book that was given to her, asserting the importance of theory in magic in relation to practice. Frieren sighs and supposes that she may have to read it to Fern at bedtime as Fern responds that she will read it herself as she is not a child. 

Frieren and Fern reach a village, and Fern inquires about collecting unusual spells. Frieren dismisses the idea, revealing there's something different this time. Frieren approaches the villagers with a question, and one of them recognizes her features. Curious, Frieren asks how he knew, and the villager leads her to the location where Qual was sealed.

As they walk, Fern questions Qual's identity, and the villager recounts that he is the Elder Sage of Corruption, responsible for terrible atrocities eighty years ago before being sealed by Himmel the Hero and his party. Frieren notes that the seal is about to break, expressing surprise at how the villager knows as she has not told anyone. The villager explains that Himmel visited the village annually until thirty years ago to check on the seal. Frieren notes Himmel's virtue, and the villager reveals that Himmel often criticized Frieren, calling her heartless and cold for neglecting to check on the demon. Frieren apologizes, but the villager continues, stating that Himmel knew Frieren wouldn't forsake the village and would return when the seal was about to break.

The three arrive at the sealing site that contains a towering Qual. Frieren observes the unstable seal and tells the villager that she will dispel the seal tomorrow and kill Qual. 

Later that night, Fern questions Frieren about whether she was the one to seal Qual and the reasons behind it. Frieren discloses that Qual was sealed due to his exceptional power. She reminisces about a memory where the Hero Party faced near defeat against Qual, an outstanding mage credited with creating Zoltraak, the first piercing magic in history. Zoltraak had the unique ability to penetrate defensive spells and magic-infused armor, directly harming the body. Frieren elaborates that in this region, 40% of adventurers and 70% of mages fell victim to Zoltraak's deadly capabilities.

Fern comments on the overwhelming power of Zoltraak, and Frieren agrees, adding that it was also the reason for Qual's downfall. Intrigued, Fern asks for clarification, but Frieren notes once again that Fern has not read the magical history book. Frieren suggests reading it to Fern, but Fern expresses her willingness to start reading immediately. Frieren, however, advises her to get some rest, assuring her that she will understand more the next day.

The next day, Frieren directs Fern to stand guard as she initiates the process of undoing Qual's seal. Qual awakens and greets Frieren, inquiring about the elapsed time. Frieren casually mentions that it's been eighty years from their perspective. Qual then questions the fate of the Demon King, and Frieren promptly discloses that the Demon King has been killed. Qual decides to avenge the Demon King and begins casting Zoltraak. Frieren instructs Fern to cast a defensive spell, and to Qual's surprise, Fern successfully blocks his spell, prompting him to acknowledge the potency of the defensive magic.

Confused, Fern questions the nature of Qual's seemingly ordinary offensive spell. Frieren reveals it to be Zoltraak, a potent spell that mages across the lands studied, analyzed and integrated into human magic, alongside new defensive spells, within a few years. She explains that advancements in magic resistance of equipment have also transformed Zoltraak from a lethal force into a mere ordinary offensive spell, highlighting how long eighty years is for humans. 

Frieren offers Qual a peaceful death if he cooperates, but undeterred, Qual instead casts defensive magic and observes how it attunes to and disperses offensive spells, realizing its significant mana consumption. He retaliates with a barrage of Zoltraak spells. Frieren instructs Fern to handle defense and steps back to cast her own spell. As Qual's spells breach Fern's defenses, he switches to a powerful frontal attack. Fern successfully responds with a frontal defensive spell. Qual notices Frieren above, curious about Frieren's ability to use flying magic, and attempts to attack her. Frieren counters with Zoltraak, destroying most of Qual's torso. In his fading moments, Qual laments the use of his own spell against him. With the battle over, Frieren lands in front of an exhausted Fern.

Later in the village, Fern is seen reading the magical history book while waiting for Frieren, who is being thanked by the villagers. The villager who led them to Qual remarks that they can finally live in peace. Frieren recognizes the villager as the brat who once flipped her skirt up from his straw hat.

A short flashback reveals the young villager flipping Frieren’s skirt up. Himmel, held back by Heiter, was outraged, asserting that he wanted to see the same thing for the longest time. As the kid runs around, Eisen told Himmel not to harm the kid, and Heiter offered to show his underwear instead, which disgusted Frieren.

As the flashback ends, Frieren notes the villager's survival, and he credits her for extending his life, thanking her for believing in Himmel's words. As Frieren and Fern depart on a carriage, Fern mentions the villagers' gratitude. Frieren clarifies that it's not directed at her but rather their belief in Himmel. Though Fern doesn’t understand, she acknowledges Himmel's belief in Frieren. Frieren smiles, patting Fern's head, and when asked about it, she dismisses it as nothing. Together, they gaze at the sky as the carriage moves away.

## Locations in Order of Appearance]

## Episode Notes]

- In the manga, the book on magical history is not recalled by Fern when talking about Frieren's shopping habits.

- In the anime, Frieren's awkwardness is expanded upon when she invites Fern out to eat.

- The depiction of human mages examining and developing Zoltraak and defense magic against it varies between the manga and the anime.

- In the anime, Qual casts defense magic while analyzing it, whereas in the manga, he merely thinks about the concept.

- In the anime, Frieren flies upwards, piquing Qual's curiosity, before she kills him, whereas in the manga, Frieren fires Zoltraak while standing on the ground.

## [ARCS] Episode 4
**The Land Where Souls Rest** ｢魂 (たましい) の眠 (ねむ) る地 (ち) , *Tamashii no nemuru chi*?｣ is the fourth episode of the *Frieren: Beyond Journey's End* anime series. It is the fourth and final part of the initial two-hour premier episode, released on September 29, 2023.

## Synopsis]

Frieren and Fern pay a visit to Eisen, who requests their help in finding the notes of Flamme the Legendary Mage.

## Plot]

27 years after Hero Himmel's passing, Frieren and Fern find themselves at the Granz Channel in the Central Lands. Guided by an elderly villager, they make their way to a neglected beach, a notorious area known for its difficulty to navigate, resulting in numerous shipwrecks over the years. The villager explains that the shore has remained unkempt due to the lack of villagers to assist with the cleanup efforts.

The villager offers Frieren a grimoire, claiming it was authored by the Great Mage Flamme. Frieren, despite recognizing it as a fake, decides to accept the villager's cleanup request. As the villager leaves, Fern questions the authenticity of the grimoire. Frieren acknowledges Fern's dedication to her studies and clarifies that books attributed to Flamme are always false. When asked why she took the request, knowing it was a fake, Frieren explains that she is simply helping someone in need, and partly doing it for her own reasons. Fern notes that it seems they will be staying in the village for a while.

Three months have passed, and winter has set in. Fern, now accustomed to village life, starts her day by buying bread in the morning before heading to the Inn. There, she finds Frieren still asleep, surrounded by a disordered pile of books on the floor, despite Fern having tidied up the day before. Urging Frieren to wake up, Fern proceeds to brush her hair, clean her after breakfast, and help her get dressed. As Frieren struggles with sleepiness, Fern ends up dragging her along to complete the shore cleanup. Working in the freezing cold, Fern questions Frieren's untidiness, expressing how she often has to wake her up, provide breakfast, and assist with dressing, essentially playing the role of Frieren's mother. Frieren responds by claiming she can manage those tasks on her own but concedes that she might end up waking up at noon if left to her own devices. Fern asserts that she has already given up hope in Frieren. When asked about how she travelled with the Hero Party, Frieren admits to frequently oversleeping but only facing consequences once. Fern comments on the party's apparent tolerance, and Frieren agrees, adding that, however, Heiter occasionally clicked his tongue at her before being stopped by Eisen and Himmel. Fern realizes that the party must have often been upset with her after all.

Frieren and Fern complete their daily cleanup, burning the collected debris. Frieren informs the elderly villager that they have a third left, anticipating finishing in time for the New Year's Festival. The villager expresses hope that Frieren will watch the sunrise this time. The next day, Fern inquires about the festival's connection to the cleanup, and Frieren explains the village tradition of watching the sunrise due to the beautiful light reflecting off the shore. When asked if she has seen it before, Frieren questions Fern's belief in her ability to wake up early.

A montage follows, showcasing Frieren and Fern's cleanup process and life in the village. The montage concludes on the day before the festival, with the successful completion of the beach cleanup. The villager thanks Frieren and Fern, inviting Frieren to join the village for the festival. Frieren agrees, prompting Fern to question her sanity, given the need to wake up before sunrise. Frieren suggests staying up all night, and when Fern asks if she's desperate to see the sunrise, Frieren responds that her lack of interest is precisely why she wants to see it, leaving Fern confused.

Late at night, Frieren reads a grimoire while Fern sleeps. Frieren reminisces about a past New Year's Festival with the Hero's Party. Himmel questions Frieren's absence, pointing out Heiter's shock that left him bedridden, but Eisen mentions that he simply drank too much. Frieren dismisses Himmel's question, stating that everyone else attended. Himmel expresses a desire for Frieren to enjoy the experience with them, insisting she would have liked it because of who she is, despite Frieren's doubts. As the memory fades, Frieren dozes off, and Fern wakes up.

Fern panics and tries to wake Frieren to avoid being late for the festival. In her sleep, Frieren calls Fern her mother before they both prepare to go out. As Fern wonders why she even bothers, Frieren, still half-asleep, thanks Fern for her help, causing her to smile.

Later, Frieren and Fern observe the sunrise. Frieren privately reflects that, despite its beauty, it was not worth waking up for, supposing that Himmel didn't understand her well after all. Intent on going home, Frieren is surprised when she looks at Fern. Fern comments on the sunrise's beauty, while Frieren dismisses it as a normal sunrise. Despite this, Fern notes that Frieren seems to be enjoying herself. Frieren explains that it's simply because Fern is smiling. Frieren admits that she would have never been able to observe the sunrise alone as the two continue to look at the sunrise.

In a flashback, the Hero's Party is depicted standing before two simple graves. Heiter asks Eisen if the graves belong to his family, and Eisen responds that they are from a time long ago when demons attacked his village. Heiter smiles and begins to pray, expressing his belief that people go to Heaven when they die. Eisen expresses doubt, revealing that he believes people turn to nothingness as they die. Frieren interjects, mentioning that until a thousand years ago, the belief in an afterlife wasn't common, and Dwarves, like Eisen, valued tradition. Frieren herself is uncertain about the afterlife, as no current magic can observe the souls of the dead to disprove or prove the existence of an afterlife. Himmel comments that it doesn't really matter, and Heiter agrees. Heiter suggests that even if the afterlife doesn't exist, it is still better to believe that people go to Heaven after trying their best in life. The Hero's Party, in agreement with Heiter's perspective, begins to pray.

28 years after the death of Hero Himmel, Frieren and Fern meet with Eisen in the Bredt region, in the Central Lands. Frieren calls out to a praying Eisen saying that she has come to hang out. Eisen asserts that Frieren is not acting like it has been thirty years. Frieren responds that a mere thirty years is nothing as Eisen scoffs and agrees.

At Eisen's home, he admits surprise to find Frieren accompanied by an apprentice. Frieren inquires if there's anything Eisen needs assistance with. Eisen discloses that he's aware Frieren asked the same question to Heiter and asserts that he is not close to his deathbed just yet. Frieren questions how he knows, prompting Eisen to reveal he often exchanged letters with Heiter.

Eisen then guides Frieren and Fern to the Voll Basin, a place that is nostalgic to Frieren, having visited it long ago. Whispering to Eisen, Fern speculates that it must have been in prehistoric times. Frieren overhears and remarks that even she isn't that old. Turning to the purpose of their visit, Eisen reveals that he is looking for notes authored by the Great Mage Flamme. Frieren accepts Eisen's request but asks whether Eisen is aware that a significant portion of Flamme's writings are fakes.

Eisen reveals that he has a lead on an authentic note, courtesy of Heiter's research from Holy City records that Flamme's notes are likely hidden in the Voll Basin. Eisen surmises that Frieren might have known about it, leading to her surprised reaction at the depth of Heiter's research. Frieren concedes, suggesting they begin the search by locating a giant tree.

Eisen, surveying the densely wooded surroundings, remarks on the abundance of trees in the area. In response, he casually notes that time is on Frieren's side, prompting Fern to start pouting. Frieren tells Eisen that she will try to finish as soon as possible as Fern would not enjoy her taking too long as Fern instructs the two to begin their search as efficiently as possible. Eisen notes that Frieren now seems mindful of others' time, a change from her previous indifference. Frieren responds that it's only because Fern can be intimidating when upset.
,

A montage ensues as the trio embarks on their search throughout Voll Basin. Later, Fern informs Frieren that she has spotted a tree growing over some ruins. As they approach the location, Frieren queries Eisen about his decision to seek Flamme's notes. Eisen responds that he simply felt sorry for Frieren and Himmel, recalling the moment when Frieren began regretting not getting to know Himmel. Eisen advises Frieren to share these sentiments directly with Himmel.

Eisen points out that Flamme's writings contain descriptions of her conversing with the dead. However, Frieren dismisses it as a fairy tale, asserting that she doesn't want to meet Himmel at the moment. Eisen inquires if Frieren doesn't wish to learn more about Himmel, disclosing that he had discussed it with Heiter. Both were certain that Frieren harbored regrets and wanted to assist her.

Eventually, the trio arrives at a giant tree and ruins that Fern observes are protected by a powerful barrier. As Fern touches the tree, Frieren reflects that even after a thousand years, her master still has her dancing in the palm of her hand.

In a flashback, Frieren expresses doubt about how a sapling will stand guard at a certain location. Frieren's master disagrees and casts magic over the sapling, declaring that it will protect the area a thousand years from now. Frieren remarks that her master would be long dead by then, but her master responds that Frieren will not. Frieren's master asserts that Frieren will make a terrible mistake and will wish she had gotten to know people better. Frieren's master tells her to return to this place when that time comes, identifying herself as the Great Mage Flamme who will be the one to help Frieren.

In the present day, Frieren's touch prompts Flamme's thousand year old tree to open, revealing a ruin containing a book. Frieren begins reading through the book, confirming its authenticity to Fern. Curious, Fern asks how Frieren is so sure, and Eisen discloses that Frieren was Flamme's best student. Responding to this revelation, Fern wonders if Frieren truly isn't from prehistoric times, as Flamme is depicted as an ancient hero in history. Eisen then asks Frieren if the book contains information on communicating with the dead. Frieren confirms, mentioning that the book was already opened to a page about that topic, making her wonder if Flamme foresaw her return a thousand years prior.

Frieren reads the page aloud, revealing Flamme's account of traveling to a place called Heaven or Aureole, the land where souls rest. There, Flamme communicated with friends who once fought alongside her. Fern asks once again if it's true, and Frieren is uncertain due to Flamme's irresponsible nature. However, Eisen asserts that Heaven exists, deeming it more convenient that way. Aureole is revealed to be located in Ende, where the Demon King's Castle resides. Eisen instructs Frieren to go to Aureole and speak with Himmel, as part of his request. Frieren accepts as she had no specific destination in mind anyway, though she expresses reluctance due to the cold around the Demon King's Castle.

Later, in a carriage, Frieren sleeps and complains about not wanting to go due to the cold. Fern questions Eisen about the castle's temperature, and he explains it is situated in the northernmost end of the continent, where the Hero Party faced numerous challenges.

Feeling the carriage situation is awkward, Fern contemplates waking Frieren, but Frieren continues to sleep on Fern's lap. Eisen asks if Frieren is a good master. Fern, uncertain, notes that Frieren often drags her around in search of magic and has shown interest in learning about Himmel and his companions. However, Fern doubts this interest applies to her personally, as Frieren took her as an apprentice only as a promise to Heiter. Despite Frieren's apparent disinterest, Fern finds it peculiar that Frieren started giving her birthday presents when they began traveling together, expressing her curiosity about Frieren's thoughts.

Eisen recalls a memory in the Royal Capital where the Hero Party watched the Era Meteors. Himmel asks Frieren if she will stay in the Capital, and she responds that she will continue traveling alone. Eisen suggests taking on an apprentice, but Frieren dismisses it as a waste of time, arguing that any apprentice would die relatively quickly even with her teachings. Eisen disagrees, stating that is not what relationships are like. Frieren maintains her stance, emphasizing that her time with the Hero Party is less than one-hundredth of her life, and supposes that Eisen should understand too. Wanting to lighten the atmosphere, Heiter encourages the rest of the party to start drinking, as it is a celebratory day, with Himmel teasing Heiter for wanting an excuse to drink.

As the memory ends, Eisen tells Fern that Frieren is a good master, prompting Fern to smile and agree as Frieren also smiles in her sleep.

Later at Eisen's home, Frieren asks Eisen if he really does not plan on coming along. Eisen confirms, reaffirming that he would only get in the way. Frieren acknowledges this and confirms to Eisen that she knows the way to Ende. As Frieren and Fern begin to take their leave, Eisen apologizes to Fern for it will be a long journey as it took the Hero Party ten years. Fern is surprised, but understands that they will be retracing the steps of Himmel and his party.

Frieren looks up as she remembers the party finally arriving at the Demon King's Castle, before turning around. Frieren tells Fern that it will be a mere ten years of adventure.

## Episode Notes]

- In the manga, Frieren and Fern sort the wood gathered from the clean-up and distribute it to the village instead of burning it right away at the beach.

- The anime depicts Frieren and Fern conversing with the elderly villager about their clean-up progress over a meal while the manga illustrates Frieren and Fern warming up by a fireplace instead.

- Eisen's house is a small cabin in the manga, whereas it is made out to be an earth dwelling in the anime.

- The depiction of Heiter searching for Flamme's notes in a library and analyzing the map of the Voll Basin in a flashback is an anime original scene that is expanded from a manga panel that shows him sitting at a desk.

- During the montage of the search for the giant tree, the scene of Eisen running over water as Fern flies Frieren over the body of water is anime original.

- The description that Flamme writes in her notes upon finding Aureole is used as an introductory quote in Episode 1.

- When Fern talks to Eisen about Frieren as a master, the anime reuses the birthday hair ornament gift scene from Episode 3 for the flashback, while in the manga, another birthday present occasion in the forest is shown. The following panel in the manga, where Frieren is shown fetching a skull and a horn from a chest, is not animated.
