## [ARCS] Episode 11
**Winter in the Northern Lands** ｢北 (きた) 側 (がわ) 諸 (しょ) 国 (こく) の冬 (ふゆ) , *Kitagawa Shokoku no fuyu*?｣ is the eleventh episode of the *Frieren: Beyond Journey's End* anime series, released on November 17, 2023.

## Synopsis]

Frieren and her companions continue their journey through the northern lands, but obstacles both natural and manmade still stand in their way.

## Plot]

As the sun rises post Aura's defeat, Frieren walks past Aura's Scales of Obedience on the ground. She prays in front of the fallen soldiers, who have finally been released from Aura's control. Fern and Stark approach her after arriving at the battlefield via carriage. Fern comments on her victory and joins her prayer. Graf Granat arrives as well and is stunned by Aura's defeat at the hands of Frieren. Upon noticing the Graf, Frieren tries to escape with Fern and Stark under the presumption that she is still the primary suspect for the death of the jail guard. The Graf tells them that they have no need to leave, and Stark tells Frieren that they have been pardoned by the Graf. Graf Granat observes the remains and comments that despite the intensity of the battle, the damage to the fallen warriors was limited. He thanks them for their service towards the fallen heroes of the Northern Lands and Frieren in particular for the respect that she has paid them.

The Graf and his soldiers continue assessing the fallen soldiers while Frieren, Fern, and Stark watch from the carriage. Frieren reminisces on her previous battle against Aura back when she was part of the Hero Party and recalls the differences, mainly that her first battle against Aura led to a lot more collateral damage. Frieren comments that due to Himmel's anger, she has since changed her ways, and Stark and Fern both comment that Himmel is good at disciplining Frieren. She tells Fern not to refer to it as parenting but nevertheless agrees with Himmel's actions. She then praises Fern and Stark for defeating Lügner and Linie. The trio banter over their injuries, though Stark, as beaten up as he is, states it is normal for a warrior. Graf Granat tells his soldiers to give the deceased their proper funerals, and one of them points out a specific soldier with a necklace of the Granat family crest. Graf Granat, realizing that he has finally found his son, profoundly expresses his gratitude to Frieren.

Back within Graf Granat's Domain, the town is busy and Graf Granat grants Frieren a requested grimoire of Flamme as a reward. He asks Frieren if she is satisfied with just the grimoire of the protective barrier magic for her efforts, given that it is not about Flamme's protective barrier. Frieren states that she is aware of it being a fake and claims that collecting grimoires is her hobby. The Graf accepts her decision and requests that she no longer refer to him with formal speech, given that he is likely much younger than her. She notes that this habit is due to the difficult time the Hero Party had on their journey to defeat the Demon King, and Fern pitches in, as Heiter had told her about the Royal Capital's emphasis on treating nobles with respect, to the point of conferring capital punishment on those who failed to be respectful. Frieren thinks back fondly to Himmel and Eisen's near-execution in the Royal Capital for casually speaking to the King. This scares Stark, who feels capital punishment is going too far since he remembers speaking rather casually with the Graf when he tried to free him back in the mansion. He criticizes the Central Lands for their uncivilized methods while mockingly referring to the Graf with formalities. Immediately after, the Graf's gardner enters the room wielding an axe, much to Stark's horror.

The gardener informs Graf Granat that he has cut down a tree as requested, and the Graf thanks him. The regent admits to the party that he only mentioned punishment when Stark spoke casually to him to get him to escape from the demons, and since no law exists that punishes individuals for speaking informally in the domain, they have nothing to worry about. Fern moves to console Stark but notices he has passed out from shock. Fern uses floating magic to carry Stark and, before they leave the room, Graf Granat advises the party to take it easy, and the townsfolk all hope to thank them for their help after hearing of Aura's defeat.

The trio reside in the town for some time to take part in a celebration of Aura's defeat. They get their wounds from the battle treated, and Fern aids around the town with her magic. Stark becomes acquainted with the townsfolk's kids and has another scare in a chance encounter with the Graf's gardener. They receive lavish gifts from Graf Granat, including a set of new winter outfits for northern travel. A large funeral for the fallen soldiers is held, which Frieren's Party attends.

In preparation to depart and travel further north, the trio meets after completing their shopping. The Graf offers to escort them out. He explains that he heard Frieren is likely heading for Ende, where the Demon King's Castle is, and he informs the party that traveling in the Northern Plateau is restricted due to rough conditions. He reveals that even adventurers require accompaniment by a first-class mage. Fern assumes they should be fine given that Frieren is with them, but her master is unaware of what determines a first-class mage. Fern explains that it is a mage qualification granted by the Continental Magic Association, and she herself obtained a third-class qualification at the Holy City before she left for their journey. Frieren voices her unfamiliarity with modern-day mage qualifications and Fern realizes Frieren may actually be an unqualified black mage, much to the elf's contempt. Frieren points out that qualifications are constantly changing due to changes in the organizations that regulate magic, and she is not able to obtain every possible qualification, which means that her Holy Emblem may also be useless.

Stark remarks that even he is aware of the Continental Magic Association given that they have existed for at least half a century. Frieren refutes the statement and thinks half a century is still very new, and the constantly changing regulations are a pain. Fern brings up that there should be a place in the Northern Lands where mages could take the first-class exam. Graf Granat affirms this and says that an exam is being held in the city of Äußerst, the largest magical city in the Northern Lands. However, traveling there will require a long journey through the Schwer Mountains. With a new destination in sight, the Graf wishes Frieren and her party safe travels as they depart Graf Granat's domain. 

On their way to the mountains, snow begins to fall as winter arrives. Frieren explains that winters in the north can get bitter, so they should be careful, as most deaths during the war against the Demon King's forces were attributed to the northern winters.

Twenty-eight years after Himmel's passing, Frieren's party reaches the Decke Region. Despite not even setting foot in the Schwer Mountains, the trio experience a severe snowstorm. While Frieren comments that they are lost, Stark collapses. Due to wind gusts, the mages are unable to carry him with magic, so they resort to carrying him conventionally, which Fern takes up. Fern bears with a mumbling, half-conscious Stark until they reach a cabin that Frieren remembers was at the foot of the mountains eighty years ago. Upon arriving, Frieren opens the door to see a tall man with pointy ears doing squats. Fern immediately drags Frieren out, apologizes for the intrusion, closes the door, and tells Frieren that they need to go somewhere else, as there is a pervert inside. Before they can get away, the man opens the door and asks if Frieren is also an elf.

Everyone heads inside the cabin and they start a conversation. The elf tells Frieren that this is the first time in three-hundred years that he has encountered another elf, and he even wondered if their species had already gone extinct. He thanks Fern for the fire she started with her magic, as he had lost his coals in the blizzard and was unable to light a fire himself. As a result, he had to resort to doing squats to warm himself up. He introduces himself as Kraft the monk, and Frieren and Fern proceed to introduce themselves and Stark. When Kraft learns that Frieren's party is traveling to Aureole, he says that their devotion is admirable, but Frieren responds that she is only half devoted. The conversation is cut short because Fern informs them that Stark's temperature is dropping.

Stark has a feverish dream, where he sees Eisen alongside a huge jumbo-berry special sundae. After a while, Stark wakes up to see that he is sleeping next to Kraft, who is keeping him warm, which alarms Stark. He nervously asks who the guy he is sleeping next to is, and Kraft takes his comment in stride and tells Stark that he should be thanking him for warming him up. Stark then compliments Kraft's body, saying that it is nice. Fern gets the wrong idea and Stark clears up the confusion, saying he was referring to his well-trained body, and he deduces that the elf is very strong. He then asks for Kraft's name and comments that he has not heard of him, but believes that he is a famous monk. Kraft then tells Stark to rest and asks Frieren and Fern to help him carry some food from his cart, which is located nearby.

They reach Kraft's stranded cart which has frozen food, and he tells them to take as much as they wish because there is plenty. Frieren looks at the Schwer Mountains and decides they should stay in the cabin a bit longer since hiking in the blizzard would be suicidal. While returning to the cabin with the supplies, Kraft asks Frieren if she knows who he is, which she negates. He figures as such, since he also knows nothing about Frieren. Fern tells him that Frieren was the mage of the Hero Party and Kraft asks what she was before. Frieren asks what he is implying, and he answers that they are elves. 

Half a year passes, with Frieren's party and Kraft spending their days in the cabin and passing the time with chores and training while waiting for the weather to improve. They have meals together, where Fern and Kraft, in devoted habit, pray before eating. Soon, Stark also joins the prayer, and finally, Frieren joins in as well. Signs of warmer weather eventually show.

One day, Frieren and Kraft are in the forest having a conversation while Kraft whittles away at a wood carving for a necklace. Kraft thanks Frieren and her party for helping him survive and asks Frieren to give the handmade necklace to Fern, complimenting her for her strong devotion to the Goddess. He thinks her piousness stems from the fact that she was raised by a priest. Frieren asks Kraft why he believes in the Goddess, claiming that apart from mythical times, she has never shown herself throughout the long history of the world. Kraft then states that Frieren must be young, since he was doubtful like her in the past, but now he truly believes in the Goddess. He says that he would be troubled if the Goddess did not exist, or rather, he *needs* the Goddess to exist. Since everyone who knew about his great accomplishments has long passed. He imagines that the Goddess would honor him by giving him praise for his life well lived. Kraft says that it is cruel that nobody will remember the tracks they left in their lives. Frieren then says that being remembered is just a wish that elves have, and Kraft rhetorically asks if that isn't Heaven as well. Kraft then changes the subject, asking Frieren to tell him about her, as if she does not believe in the Goddess, he will honor her himself. This causes Frieren to recall a memory of when she was traveling with the Hero Party.

In the flashback, Himmel and Eisen were surrounded by happy children while Frieren sat at a table talking to Heiter. Frieren said she never imagined Heiter would donate towards the reconstruction of an orphanage, so the fact he did surprised her. Heiter told Frieren that he was also an orphan, and he believed that the Goddess would honor him for living purely and righteously. Frieren disagreed with this and asked what the corrupt priest is saying while getting drunk. Heiter suddenly asked her if she had anyone to honor her, and she asked why. Heiter explained that it seemed that she does not believe in the Goddess and that if she told him about herself, he will honor her in the Goddess's place. Frieren said that she has been living leisurely until now, so she has not done anything worthy of being honored. Heiter stated that despite this, she had dedicated her life to constantly limiting her mana. Frieren was surprised that Heiter noticed, but she remarked that her story was not an interesting one. Heiter said that he does not mind and her story would be good for future reference, since his child might become a mage. Frieren questioned Heiter about his statement, since priests are supposed to be single for life, which made Heiter laugh.

Back in the present, Frieren wonders why so many strange people believe in the Goddess as she watches Stark and Fern clear the cabin's roof of snow. She says to Kraft that she will pass on his offer, since she already has somebody to praise her. Kraft thinks that she has good friends and tells Frieren to treasure them. This makes Frieren pause for a moment before she explains that her friend is already in Heaven. Kraft says that means Frieren will see him again one day, to which Frieren agrees.

Later, once warmer weather has set in, Frieren's party and Kraft part ways and continue their separate adventures. Kraft tells Frieren that he does not consider this their final farewell before they split up, and that he will see her again, however many centuries later.

## Episode Notes]

- The anime shows a closeup of Aura's Scales of Obedience lying on the ground, the only thing remaining of the demon. This closeup is not included in the manga.

- When showcasing the return to normalcy within Graf Granat's Domain, the anime shows a boy petting a cat before the meeting between Frieren's Party and Graf Granat. Although this has no corresponding panel in the manga, a cat is part of a panel during the montage depicting the moments Frieren's party spends while celebrating Aura's defeat with the townsfolk. The scene of the boy petting the cat was also used in Episode 8, when Stark and Fern have a meal and plan to get Frieren out of the prison.

- As with other flashbacks of this scene, the anime represents the flashback of Himmel and Eisen facing capital punishment through an executioner swinging a sword, but in the manga, Himmel and Eisen are depicted with their heads fixated in a guillotine.

- During the montage after Frieren's party's audience with Graf Granat, the anime has an original frame showing the Graf being in thought while in his son's room with the sword.

- In the manga, a map of the northern continent is in the background when the Graf sees Frieren's party off to the gates and tells them that travel in the north is restricted. The anime does not adapt it to this part of the conversation, but it is shown later when the Graf informs the mages about Äußerst. The manga also has a part of the map shown in this scene.

- When Fern shows Frieren her third-class mage certificate granted by the Continental Magic Association, the text on the certificate on the initial aired version of the episode says "Certificate of Third-Rank Magician." This was changed in the final blu-ray version of the episode to be "Certificate of Third-Class Mage" instead.

- In the manga, Frieren has already taken a step into the cabin before getting yanked out by Fern, while she just apologizes in the anime for the interruption.

- The anime scene of Stark's dream while being warmed up is extended compared to the manga by adding the illusion of Eisen and a jumbo-berry special. In the manga, Stark only mentions the dream while he is unconscious and being dragged through the snow by Fern.

- The manga panels shows Kraft, Frieren, and Fern carrying the supplies from Kraft's cart through a snowstorm, however, the anime has the mages use a spell that makes things float to transfer the items once better weather conditions arrive.

- The iconography of the Goddess of Creation on the mantelpiece of the chimney in the cabin is anime original. However, in the manga, Kraft and Fern engage in discussion of the Holy Scripture, which is not part of the montage in the anime. Additionally, the manga does not show Stark and Frieren joining the prayer in succession before the meal.

- The anime includes an original scene at the end of the flashback to Frieren's conversation with Heiter, which consists of Stark catching Fern when she slips on the cabin roof while clearing the roof of snow with him.

- Stark and Fern shout out to Kraft in the distance after they part ways, and this is not included in the manga.

## References]

## Site Navigation]


## [ARCS] Episode 12
**A Real Hero** ｢本 (ほん) 物 (もの) の勇 (ゆう) 者 (しゃ) , *Honmono no yūsha*?｣ is the twelfth episode of the *Frieren: Beyond Journey's End* anime series, released on November 24, 2023.

## Synopsis]

Deep in the mountains of the northern lands, Frieren and her party arrive at the Village of the Sword, where they have another job to do.

## Plot]

Twenty-nine years after Himmel the Hero's passing, Frieren's Party are in the Northern Lands, specifically, the Schwer Mountains. Stark and Fern travel a bit ahead, while Frieren has a hard time with the cold and falls asleep with a nose dive into the snow. Fern notices this and returns to pick her up. Stark offers to carry Frieren, but Fern shuts him down.

While being carried, Frieren has a flashback of the Hero Party, where she remembers their audience with the King and their subsequent departure to defeat the Demon King. Eisen was surprised at the mere ten copper coins granted by the King for their journey, and Heiter explained that many adventurers had unsuccessfully tried to defeat the Demon King. Himmel supposed that their lack of funds just means they have the opportunity to earn more on their journey, and he explained that it feels like they are going on a real adventure, to which Heiter agreed.

Himmel took out and admired his sword, and Frieren identified it as the "Sword of the Hero," but Heiter corrected her and clarified that the sword is just a replica. Himmel recalled the events leading to him receiving the sword: the sword was gifted to him as a token of gratitude by a merchant he saved from a monster, and the merchant described it as a sword for a hero. Frieren asked him if that was why he wanted to become a hero, but Himmel denied this, and he explained that he wanted to prove Heiter wrong, as when they were younger, Heiter told him that he would only become a fake hero with a fake sword. Therefore, he resolved to become a real hero and acquire the real Sword of the Hero and defeat the Demon King. As they continued traveling, Himmel joked that Heiter was a fake priest who only drank, and they all laugh and move on, except for Frieren, who is speechless and fascinated when Himmel turned back to her with a smile.

Back in the present, Frieren wakes up and instructs Fern, who is currently carrying her, to press forward, as she finds the current landscape familiar. She mentions that she underestimated the weather in the mountains, however, their destination—a village—should be nearby. Fern asks if Frieren can walk, but she refuses. Stark offers to carry her, but Fern rejects his offer and continues carrying Frieren until she eventually starts walking on her own. The snowstorm subsides, and the trio notice their destination in view as they pass by a broken-down building. When they reach the fortified village, they are welcomed to the Village of the Sword by its chief—a young girl who introduces herself as the 49th village chief.

While walking with the chief, Frieren asks what the destroyed building was, and the chief tells Frieren that it was a hunter's cabin in the past that was destroyed by the Lord of the Mountains. As Frieren tries to recall if there was a "Lord of the Mountains" in the past, Stark recognizes the name of the Village of the Sword, and Fern asks if he was aware of it. Stark explains that this village protects the "Sword of the Hero," a famous sword allegedly embedded by the Goddess of Creation, and it was said to have been extracted by Himmel eighty years prior, the first to do so since it was placed. The village chief recites the legend of the sword, which describes it as something that can only be pulled by the hero that drives out the great calamity. Fern clarifies that Himmel was the one who pulled out the sword, and Stark confirms. Stark is confused about how Fern does not know such a famous story, and Fern replies that Heiter never mentioned it to her.

Frieren's party accompany the village chief into a building, where Frieren sits by the fireplace to warm up. The chief recites the will of her grandmother, a past village chief, and she acts out her grandmother's anger towards Frieren given the elf was late on her promise to return half a century later to help protect the village. Frieren says that she expected it would be safe for 80 years, but the village chief stresses that she still has to fulfill her duty. Fern asks what the chief meant by duty, and Frieren tells her it is monster extermination. The chief explains that the "Ruler of the Mountains" has been troublesome, and Frieren decides they will start on the task the next day.

The next day, Frieren's party starts to defeat many wolf-like monsters, and the chief applauds their efforts. Fern asks why they did not issue a subjugation request to adventurers, and the chief replies that they could, but Frieren ends her reply with the statement that Himmel is the Hero, leaving Fern confused. Stark sees more monsters congregating at the entrance of a cave and proceeds to kill them. As he turns to talk to Frieren, he is pushed down by the Lord of the Mountains. The chief confirms that this monster is the Lord, and Frieren is unimpressed that, within eighty years, the monster would consider itself a Lord. She faces the creature and demands Stark to move if he still can. Stark complies and cuts the monster's arm off, which prompts the monster to take a swing at Frieren with its remaining claw, but Fern casts a spherical defense spell around herself and Frieren. Frieren praises her and then proceeds to exterminate the monster with a blast of offense magic.

Stark sits down in front of the cave entrance and confronts Frieren about what is inside it, which is the "Sword of the Hero," still embedded within a rock. She tells him that it was the reason that monsters are attracted by the cave, as they cannot resist the urge to destroy the blade even though the sanctuary is protected by a powerful barrier. Stark says that he did not mean the monsters, and Frieren, understanding his confusion, explains that Himmel could not pull the sword out as she recalls when the Hero's Party visited the same cave eighty years ago.

In Frieren's flashback, Himmel unsuccessfully retrieved the sword. The village chief at the time—the grandmother of the present one—remarked that he must not be a true hero either, as he failed alongside those that previously attempted to remove the sword. Heiter tried to console Himmel, but before he could, Himmel stated that it was fine if he was a fake hero. He reassured his determination to defeat the Demon King and bring peace, and as long as he is able to achieve this feat, it will not matter if he is a fake or real hero.

In the present, Frieren describes that Himmel was ultimately able to accomplish his goal, and even without the sword, he had proved that he could save the world and that he was a real hero. Fern asks why this was kept a secret, and Frieren replies that it was probably the doing of those who wanted Himmel to be the hero. She explains that unsavory anecdotes would be detrimental to his story, as heroes are glorified by future generations and their stories eventually become unrecognizable. Frieren, Fern, and the chief head back to the village, but Stark stays behind and contemplates their discussion. He looks at the Sword of the Hero stuck in the stone and has a sudden memory about a man with red hair standing in front of a burning house.

Later, Frieren's party prepares to continue on their journey. The village chief thanks them in a manner her grandmother would express and asks Frieren not to be late next time. Frieren's party subsequently departs from the village.

That same year, Frieren's party travels further in the Northern Lands and arrives at the Appetit Region. They reach a town and settle at an inn, deciding to relax for the rest of the day. Frieren chooses to read grimoires in her room and Fern prepares to head out to explore the shops on her own. Before Fern leaves, Frieren suddenly remembers that it is Stark's eighteenth birthday. Fern panics, as she has not arranged a gift for him. When Frieren suggests simply buying one while she shops, Fern mentions that she is unsure about what Stark likes. Frieren teases her for her uncertainty, which Fern blames on her.

Fern asks Frieren what she intends to gift him, and Frieren excitedly jumps out of bed to open her suitcase and says she planned something special. She holds up a potion and reveals that it is capable of dissolving clothes, and she smirks while saying her master told her that men would be very happy to receive such a gift. Fern is shocked and disgusted by the idea and takes the bottle out of Frieren's hand. Much to Frieren's dismay, Fern opens it and pours the contents onto her, melting her clothes, and Fern comments that this vulgar purchase should have been returned back when bought. She promptly leaves, slamming the door. A devastated Frieren grumbles that the drug was precious and wraps herself in a blanket. As she thinks about a new gift for Stark, she goes over the contents of her suitcase once more. Her attention falls on a ring, which she picks up and stares at for a moment. She then notices a slip of paper, which gives her an idea.

Fern chooses to investigate what to gift Stark, and upon discovering his empty room, she begins asking the townsfolk for help locating him. Multiple individuals recall encountering him after he had helped them with various tasks, such as a merchant lady whose cart he helped push, some kids he played with, a child with a cat he retrieved from a tree, and a cattle breeder whose cattle he helped round up. After hearing these stories of Stark being courteous, Fern reinforces her idea that Frieren was being inconsiderate for generalizing his personality. Right after, she discovers him on a bench. As she approaches him, he loudly points out vulgar cloud shapes to himself. This causes her to retreat to a house corner, and she realizes that Stark has childish thoughts. He comments out loud that he will tell Fern about his cloud discoveries, and Fern is unsure how to respond. Eventually, she resolves to approach him and addresses him from behind. He turns around and begins to tell her about the clouds but falls silent upon seeing Fern's facial expression.

Fern invites him on a walk, and as Stark asks her about why she was angry, she ignores him. She is unsure how to bring up his birthday and decides to ask directly. Surprised, he questions her if she would be gifting him something, but his words anger her and she tells him to forget about it. Stark plays his words off as a joke and reflects on how he has never received birthday gifts growing up, even from his family or his master, and he has come to accept this. He explains that after all, he was raised in a village full of warriors, and they did not value weaklings.

Stark thinks back to his childhood and recalls a scene where his father scolded a handful of warriors with blemished white cloaks and expressed that they should look up to Stark's brother, Stoltz, who stood uninjured in front of a defeated boar-like monster with his white cloak still pristine. Stark's father claimed that Stoltz is the strongest and the pride of the village, and as he walked by a young Stark training, he considered the boy a failure in comparison.

As it started raining, Stark's father headed home first, but Stoltz stayed behind to help his brother. As Stark practiced his sword technique, Stoltz took the initiative to train his younger brother and was patient with him, praising him for his concentration and giving him pointers on how to improve. In the present, Stark remembers Stoltz was the only individual who was like that with him. Stark recalls another memory, where a demon that had attacked the village had a standoff against the village's warriors. Upon realizing the gravity of the situation, the young Stark turned away and fled the attack. 

After thinking back to his past, Stark remarks that he abandoned Stoltz and fled during the demon's attack. He blames himself for running and thinks that his family was right to never have celebrated his birthday. Stark then remembers the Sword of the Hero and mentions that Himmel would not run away in the same circumstances.

After hearing Stark's story, Fern tells him that he should go with her to pick a present and not concern himself with his past, as she only knows the Stark that has fought back and never fled. Stark reminds her that he may flee in the future, but Fern rebutes him and tells him that she and Frieren will not let him do so. She says she will pick out his present on her own if he does not come along with her, and after he reluctantly agrees, they spend time in the shops choosing his present. Stark ends up picking a silver bracelet, and the two of them return back to the inn, with Stark sporting the bracelet.

Frieren welcomes them back and tells them they are late as she serves giant hamburger steaks, fried over an open fire. Fern questions her intentions, but before Frieren replies, Stark says that this is how birthdays are celebrated. Stark mentions that despite never receiving presents from Eisen, his master would always make him these steaks for his birthday. Frieren asks if Eisen has ever told Stark the idea behind it and remarks that warriors are awkward, and given that she is too, she understands Eisen's point of view. Frieren tells Stark that those who are awkward cannot properly express their thoughts unless they are put into words.

Frieren refers back to a time the Hero Party was camping at night, and Eisen was busy with frying massive hamburger steaks on a grill. When Frieren asked why he would cook these steaks on their birthdays, the dwarf explains that it was a regional custom to thank warriors for their hard work. Himmel commented that the Hero Party's members aren't warriors, but Eisen replied that he defined a warrior as anyone who puts in their best effort. Stark muses over Frieren's explanation and Eisen's statement, and he thinks back to one of his birthdays, where Stoltz had also secretly made a hamburger steak for him. He then remembers the night of the demon attack, where Stoltz had instructed him to escape and live. Frieren cites Eisen for the steak recipe and asks about its taste, and Stark replies that he enjoys it.

After their meal, Frieren reveals the potion that dissolves clothes and points out there is a little left. An upset Fern replies that she will pour the remainder onto Frieren's head again. The curious Stark then asks what the potion was, but he receives a flat reply from Fern, who calls him a pervert.

## Episode Notes]

- The volume extra from Chapter 25 included in the episode.
- The volume extra from Chapter 26 included in the episode.
1/2
- The anime begins with Frieren's Party traveling, while Chapter 25 of the manga has the Hero Party flashback as the start.
The scene of Frieren's collapse and Stark's first offer to carry Frieren is anime original.

- When Himmel describes how he got his sword, a panel of him saving the merchant as a kid from a bird-like monster is shown in the manga, and this scene is not adapted by the anime.

- The anime includes two additional scenes in the episode based on volume extras from the manga:
The volume extra from Chapter 25: Fern carries Frieren through the snow on the Schwer Mountains, with Frieren saying that it smells nice.

- The volume extra from Chapter 26: Frieren gives Stark the potion, and when Stark asks what it is, Fern calls him a pervert.

- The memories of Himmel that Frieren has while talking about his legacy anime original.

- The memory of Stoltz that Stark has while sitting in front of the cave is anime original.

- As Frieren goes through her suitcase in the anime, she looks at a ring with the mirrored-lotus flower motif before spotting Eisen's recipe. This is an anime original scene and alludes to Episode 14.

- The potion that only dissolves clothes was first introduced by Fern, who remarked that it was an unnecessary purchase in Episode 3.

- Eisen's recipe and Frieren's process of making the hamburger steak is extended upon in the spin-off *Frieren in the Kitchen*.

## [ARCS] Episode 13
**Aversion to One's Own Kind** ｢同 (どう) 族 (ぞく) 嫌 (けん) 悪 (お) , *Dōzoku ken'o*?｣ is the thirteenth episode of the *Frieren: Beyond Journey's End* anime series, released on December 1, 2023.

## Synopsis]

While passing by a village in the woods of the northern lands, Frieren and party meet Sein, a gifted priest who is nonetheless corrupt enough to give even Heiter a run for his money. But what happened in his past? 

## Plot]

Twenty-nine years after Himmel the Hero's passing, Frieren's Party arrives at the Alt Woods in the Northern Lands. Frieren goes to gather herbs alone and encounters a man. She introduces herself as an adventurer, and the man tells her his backstory, as he wanted to become an adventurer himself a long time ago. However, he now recognizes that he was simply following a childish dream. 

The man remembers how during his childhood, he had a good friend, an energetic boy that had the mannerisms of a gorilla. His friend was a caring individual, and they would frequently join each other on little adventurers, such as climbing a large tree together. However, after the man became a young adult, he slowly started to forget his dream. His friend invited him to become adventurers together, but he rejected his offer. Now, a decade later, the man acknowledges that he regrets his decision and thinks about how things would have been different if he had taken his friend's hand.

Frieren asks why he would tell her such a story, and the man states that since the harvest festival of his village is arriving, he was tasked by his older brother to gather herbs. However, he got stuck in a bottomless swamp and is now slowly sinking in, and he thinks he is done for. As he continues sinking, he reaches out with his hand and desperately tries to convince Frieren to help him. Frieren requests for more time to think about it, and she ultimately refuses, as the man's hand is dirty from being covered in mud. As she tries to recall a spell to pull someone out of a bottomless swamp, Fern arrives to check on Frieren. Frieren ends up remembering the spell, and she frees the man.

After reuniting with Stark, Frieren's party accompanies the man to his village. Fern apologizes for the trouble Frieren caused and states that she will scold her. As an expression of gratitude, the man invites Frieren's party to his village, but they decline as they need to replenish their supplies and prefer to reach a major town by the end of the day. He understands and warns them of dangerously venomous creatures. Stark confirms with enthusiasm that he heard his advice. However, shortly after they part ways with the man, Stark gets bitten in the arm by a venomous snake while looking at berries on a bush. Fern is stunned and voices her disappointment, but her irritation is diverted when Stark's nose starts bleeding.

Frieren applies a spell that identifies poison, but she is unable to analyze it properly since she is not a priest. As she cannot recognize the reaction, the party decides to get him diagnosed in a church. Fern confirms that they do not have not enough mana to fly to the next town, so they decide to head back to the previous village. Stark initially refuses, as he thinks he can tough the poison out like his master. Frieren recalls that Eisen was indeed unfazed after he was struck with three arrows coated with poison strong enough to knock out a dragon, appalling Heiter, but Fern thinks Eisen's constitution is just out of the ordinary. Heiter had once told her that twenty percent of adventurers would die by poison, so Fern urges them to head back by utilizing flying magic.

Frieren's party arrives at the village's church, where they meet the church father, the village's local priest. He chillingly states that it is too late for Stark as the snake bite would only be treatable during the initial stage. However, he considers that perhaps his younger brother might be able to cure him. At that moment, the man from before, named Sein, enters the church's main hall to talk to his elder brother, the village's priest, and recognizes Frieren's party. He promptly and effortlessly treats Stark by putting a hand on his shoulder and applying detoxification magic before leaving to help at the plaza.

When the church father asks Frieren what she thinks of Sein, Frieren points out the Holy Symbol emblem around the neck of the church father, which she mentions is only granted to the very best priest of a region by the Holy City. Frieren notes that Sein is a healing expert who has outstanding talent, as he could instantly cure a poison that even the superior priest of the region deemed incurable, which would make him a genius. The village priest says he knows about Frieren because Heiter told stories when he came to the village to award the emblem, but he does not compare himself to his younger brother. He tells her that their parents passed away early and that he took care of Sein. Although Sein used to tell his brother about how he wanted to become an adventurer, he changed when he became an adult. Sein's elder brother then asks Frieren to take him away from the village, as he believes Sein has been searching for someone to push him to revitalize his dream.

Back at the inn, both Stark and Fern are in favor of Sein's brother's proposal, as it would be beneficial to have a priest in the party. Frieren is uneasy, stating cryptically that she has an aversion against her own kind. Stark does not understand her reasoning, but he nonetheless sets out to recruit Sein, leaving Fern and Frieren to go downstairs and visit the bar where Sein spends time. He finds Sein playing a card game with two other men while also drinking and smoking at the tavern. Stark comments on the situation looking corrupt, however, Sein says it is a way to get to know people. He invites the boy to have a seat and take part in the game. If he wins the gambling match, Sein promises to join the party.

Stark's scream interrupts Fern's reading in bed upstairs. She wakes up Frieren and both rush to ascertain Stark's situation. The mages find the young man stripped bare down to his underwear wailing outside the tavern. Fern states that the situation looks terrible and is surprised that not only are all of Stark's belongings missing, but Sein, who is sitting against a wall smoking, has also been stripped after losing all his belongings. Sein explains that the village chief beat both of them, and he asks the party to not judge him, as all adults are dirty. When Frieren asks Sein to join their party, Sein tells Frieren to find someone else, as he thinks it is too late for him to pursue the path of an adventurer.

Sein's remarks remind Frieren of when Himmel first set out to recruit her. In a flashback, Himmel, accompanied by Eisen and Heiter, invites Frieren to defeat the Demon King as part of the Hero Party. She states that she has not fought a demon in over five hundred years, so she has forgotten how to do so. She believes that she must have been afraid and deferred the decision for too long to fight the Demon King, and now that enough years have passed, it is already too late. Himmel tells Frieren that he is talking about the present, which she recites verbatim to Sein.

Upon hearing this, Sein is briefly reminded of his childhood friend, but he still refuses and tells Frieren that she could not understand his feelings. Frieren rebutes him and says that his response tells her everything she needs to know, and since she does not like him, she has unwaveringly decided to make him a party member no matter what. Sein fails to understand this logic and expresses that he is scared by the conviction Frieren demonstrates.

Shortly after the conversation between Sein and Frieren, Fern goes to retrieve Stark and Sein's belongings. She visits the village chief and apologizes for the trouble the men caused him, however, the chief returns all of the men's belongings for free and wishes her a nice stay during the village's harvest festival. Fern returns Stark and Sein's belongings, but not without an expression of her disdain towards both of them. After Fern leaves, Sein questions what made her so upset, and Frieren explains that Fern did not like how Stark got stripped of all his belongings.

Back at the inn, Fern complains about how awful she finds gamblers, especially Sein, as he is a priest. Frieren remarks that she is unsure about priests that drink, but Fern states alcohol is the best medicine, which makes Frieren think that Heiter gave Fern awful teachings. Frieren returns to discussing Sein and says that whether or not they make Sein an ally, she still wants to support him on his journey to become an adventurer, as that is what Himmel would have done.

Frieren's party stays in the village over the next few days and tries to recruit Sein every day. Sein remarks that Frieren's eyes seem similar to his old friend's, which were filled with hopes and dreams, as she unrelentingly pushes him to go on an adventure with her party. He remembers a scene from the past where his childhood friend told him he will go explore the Northern Lands and that he will return for the next harvest festival in three years. He told Sein that he can decide then if he wanted to go on an adventure with him.

After many failed attempts to recruit Sein, Frieren's party goes to the church and consults Sein's older brother about what Sein likes. He tells them about the priests fondness for alcohol, tobacco, and gambling. This prompts Fern to say that Heiter was a serious priest after all, but Frieren disagrees. Sein's brother says Sein is also interested in older women, which gives Frieren's party an idea. Sein later comes in and has a small conversation with the brother, and as he leaves the church, Stark goes after him. He talks to Sein outside and asks if he wants to travel with an older lady. Sein answers becoming an adventurer when he was a kid was just for that.

When Sein asks where the older lady is, Frieren reveals herself, saying that as an elf, she is a much older lady. However, Sein is distressed by the thought and states that Frieren could not be considered a lady. Frieren then tries to seduce him by blowing him a kiss, a seduction technique she learned from her master, but it has no effect on Sein, and he instead considers it childish. Fern and Stark, however, are embarrassed by Frieren's action, which makes Sein unimpressed. Frieren is disappointed by this outcome, as she recalls that she was able to make Himmel faint when she tried it on him, earning her a stinging remark by Eisen. The elf finds it strange that Sein is not affected, and Stark supposes that Sein is a still a priest despite how corrupt he is.

Sein tells Frieren that she should stop now, as he has no intention of becoming an adventurer. Frieren asks why he does not want to track down his best friend, and Sein addresses his brother, saying he would understand him. Sein tells her that his childhood friend said he would return in three years, but it has been ten years since, so he must already be dead. Frieren points out that Sein is giving up before he has even gone to pursue him and it has only been a mere ten years. She adds that if Sein does not go now, he would regret it in the future. As Sein asks why he should go now, Frieren restates that she is talking about the present. This statement seems to move Sein, but he still refuses, saying that the reason why he refuses to leave the village is the same as ten years ago: he cannot abandon his older brother.

When his brother asks what he means, Sein shares that when he was younger, he overheard a conversation between his brother and Heiter when the bishop came to visit. Sein heard Heiter tell his elder brother that with his talent, he could serve as a priest at the Holy City, and Sein could come with him. However, Sein's elder brother declined and stated that he was content living in the village and that he cannot take Sein's hometown away from him, as the boy had already lost his parents at a very young age. Heiter accepted his decision and decided that since he came to the village anyways, he might as well tell Sein about some of his adventures.

In the present, Sein concludes that his older brother stayed behind in the village for his sake. Sein's brother, upon hearing this, becomes angry and slaps Sein. He tells him that they are not the same, as he has not once regretted the decision he made. He asks Sein how long he is planning to drown himself in regret, leaving Sein to mull over his words.

Later that day, while Frieren's party are at a river, Sein approaches them and reveals that he apologized to his older brother. He tells Frieren that it is the first time his brother has ever raised a hand on him, and it also was the first time he saw such an expression from him. Sein announces to Frieren that he has decided to become an adventurer to pursue his friend, as after all, it has only been a mere ten years since he left. Sein explains that he wants to make his childhood dream come true and states that he will travel with Frieren's party partway until he finds his old friend.

Frieren's party prepare to depart the village, now with Sein added as a party member, and they bid farewell to the villagers. Sein asks what the destination of their journey is, and Frieren replies Heaven. Sein says that anyone could go there by dying, but Fern retorts that she wonders if even Sein could go there as well. Sein is baffled about Fern's straightforwardness, and Stark consoles him.

## Episode Notes]

- The anime shows how the venomous snake bit Stark, while in the manga, Stark is only shown with the snake hanging from his arm after it bites him. The manga also shows Frieren stepping on the snake before Fern tries to stop the bleeding.

- In the manga, when deciding if they can reach the next town, Frieren checks a map.

- A flashback of a younger Sein climbing to the top of the church's bell tower's top with his brother looking up is original to the anime. The flashback in the manga shows Sein walking with his brother instead.

- In the manga, the inn where Frieren's Party stays and the tavern seem to be two distinct places, while the anime appears to depict them to be within the same building.

- The anime includes an additional scene based on a volume extra from Chapter 27 in the manga: After Frieren and Fern find Stark and Sein after the two men lose their belongings, Fern puts her coat around Stark to keep him warm.

- The anime shows Fern getting Stark and Sein's belongings back for free from the village chief, while in the manga, Fern purchases the items back from a merchant for cheap due to a sale during the harvest festival.

- In the anime, as Sein says he will join Frieren's party, Stark catches a fish. This does not correspond to a panel in the manga, but the scene appears to be similarly depicted on the cover of Chapter 28.

## [ARCS] Episode 14
**Privilege of the Young** ｢若 (わか) 者 (もの) の特 (とっ) 権 (けん) , *Wakamono no tokken*?｣ is the fourteenth episode of the *Frieren: Beyond Journey's End* anime series, released on December 8, 2023.

## Synopsis]

The party arrives in a large and lively town with a bustling shopping district that Frieren once visited with Himmel, but something seems to have come up between Fern and Stark.

## Plot]

Twenty-nine years after Himmel's passing, Frieren's Party arrives at the Raad Region in the Northern Lands, where they visit a lively town filled with shops. Frieren recognizes the town as one the Hero Party had visited before, and she briefly recalls their experience, which includes Heiter delight towards the abundance of bars and Himmel's invitation to go shopping with Frieren. In the present, she looks at a clock tower in the distance. Stark calls out to her, and she goes to catch up with the rest of her party.

In an inn, Stark tearfully exclaims that Fern is too critical to him. He tells Frieren and Fern that he has had enough and loudly proclaims that he is returning to his master, slamming the door on his way out. In the hallway, Sein watches him angrily leave while complaining about Fern. Frieren follows Stark out the door and encounters Sein, who has only witnessed the aftermath of the argument and asks if Stark and Fern are having a lovers' quarrel. Frieren sits with a sulking Fern on the bed and explains that today is Fern's birthday, but Stark failed to prepare a present for her. Frieren believes that Fern went overboard, as she refused to listen to anything Stark said. Sein inputs that he too has no gift for Fern, as men typically do not make a big deal out of anniversaries like birthdays. Fern's anger erupts and she stands up to kick Sein's shins, causing Sein to say he will go buy Fern a gift. As he lights a cigarette, Sein expresses that he feels sorry for Stark and tells Fern that for a boy of Stark's age, dealing with girls is hard and can affect him emotionally. When Sein heads out, he advises Fern that she should pursue Stark. Fern is further urged to do so by Frieren, and after she contemplates the idea, Fern heads out.

Stark sits despondently at the base of a statue of Himmel and looks at his bracelet. Fern finds him and watches him from behind a building, uncertain about what to do. Meanwhile, Sein searches for a present for Fern and sets his eyes on a pouch with a butterfly design from a vendor, noting that Fern also has a butterfly hair ornament. Fern approaches him and comments that she finds the pouch cute. Sein wonders if the pouch is not to Fern's taste, but Fern refutes him and claims that she finds the pouch unpleasant as it gives the impression that Sein is experienced with women.

Sein then asks Fern if she managed to find Stark. Fern states that she saw him at the plaza, but she does not finish her statement, leading Sein to deduce that Fern was unable to talk to him. He notes that her youth makes her incapable of handling boys the same age as her, but he can see that she does not actually hate Stark. He requests that Fern pick whichever item she wants for her gift or choose a different store. Fern smiles and tells him it is alright, prompting him to say that he will choose something then. As he continues looking, Sein advises Fern that even if Stark failed to prepare her a gift, he still thinks she was too hard on him, as Stark is not the most aware guy and probably does not even remember his own birthday. Fern explains that she gave Stark a present on his birthday, but Sein calls her out on the fact that he picked something out with her together for him. Fern is surprised that Sein was able to figure that out, but Sein tells her that it is rare for people to reject an offer to pick whatever present they would like. After this, he grabs the pouch with the butterfly motif and buys it from the shop owner. He hands the gift to Fern and encourages her to make up with Stark by vocalizing her thoughts and properly express them to him.

Fern approaches Stark, who is still at the plaza, and Stark apologizes to Fern before she can voice her words. He explains that he wanted to find something together, but he was unsure if she would like the idea. Fern tells him she would not be upset with him for proposing the idea and apologizes in return for treating him harshly. They reconcile and walk down the street to explore the town.

Frieren watches Fern and Stark from a rooftop, and she is soon joined by Sein. He tells her that she should not be spying on Fern and Stark, but Frieren reminds him that he is doing the same. Sein comments that the two have managed to make up, and he expresses that Fern and Stark being able to argue is a privilege only young individuals can experience, as adults would have learned to avoid conflicts of this nature. He tells Frieren that she has it rough dealing with the two kids, but Frieren struggles to comprehend what he means about understanding relationships, which causes Sein retort that Frieren must also be a kid. Sein tells Frieren that Fern came to him to ask for advice, and he wonders who she is comparing him to. Frieren explains that Heiter was the one who raised Fern, and Sein is uncertain about being compared to a man he holds in such high regard. Frieren cites Heiter's unpleasant sides and points out that Heiter was a corrupt priest, but Sein views him as the ideal adult.

Frieren thinks back to Heiter's last years, when she was with him and Fern. She said to Heiter that he had matured, and he acknowledged that he had grown old. However, Heiter felt that his mind had barely changed since he was a child and that instead of him being an actual adult, he just pretended to be one, and he had to do so to provide emotional support to Fern as a good role model. After Heiter said that children need praise, Frieren asked who would praise Heiter for his efforts. He mentioned that the Goddess would do so when he gets to Heaven, but Frieren remarked that she will praise him now and started patting him on the head. Heiter expressed the pleasantness of her action, and he told her that when he sees the Goddess, he will ask her to also praise Frieren.

Back in the present, Frieren starts patting Sein's head. He asks her what her intention is, and she tells him that he is doing a good job as an adult. Sein voices his disappointment, as he would have appreciated an older women comforting him instead. Meanwhile, Stark and Fern browse the streets of the town as Stark tries to find a present for Fern.

After leaving the Rohr Road town, Frieren's party catches a ride on a horse-drawn carriage that moves through the Bande Woods in the Northern Lands. Frieren thanks the driver for taking them along, as wagons are not common in the area. The driver reveals that he is a merchant who runs an accessories shop, and he asks if the party would be interested in checking out his goods. Frieren responds that he is a good salesman, but she is not interested. As she asks if Fern would be interested, Frieren notices Fern wearing a new bracelet. Frieren compliments the design and mentions that she had once been gifted a ring from Himmel that has the same design.

Frieren begins digging through her suitcase in search of the ring, but she is unable to find it due to the unkempt state of her luggage, which Fern chastises her for. She finally finds the ring, however, immediately after, the wagon is lifted into the air by an enormous aerial monster.

Frieren apologizes for letting down her guard and not detecting the monster earlier, and she comments on the ability of bird monsters to cunningly mask their mana. Stark suggests that they fight the bird and use flying magic to land the wagon, but Frieren asks if he has ever seen a flying carriage before and points out that humans have only recently been able to fly in the last forty years by copying flying magic from demons. Thus, mankind's version of flying magic cannot be used freely, as its principles are still unknown, and objects larger than humans can only be made to fly for a short period of time, which is not enough for them to safely land. With their options limited, Frieren proposes they simply escape by flying. Fern is asked to take Sein while she herself takes the merchant.

Stark asks what he is supposed to do, and Frieren tells him to jump down, but Stark reminds her that he will fall to his death. Frieren comments that he, as a warrior, would not die from falling from that height, with which Stark vehemently disagrees. Frieren recalls how Eisen could fall from any height without sustaining any injuries, shocking Heiter, but Fern reminds Frieren that this only shows how far from normal Eisen was. Fern suggests making the wagon float right before it hits the ground. Frieren calculates if they can cancel out their fall, as they must break the momentum or the wagon would be crushed, much to Stark's dismay.

Sein points out that they should make their decision soon, as the bird monster hunts its prey by slamming it into the ground. Frieren agrees and immediately heads out to cast an offensive spell at the monster, decapitating it. Subsequently, the wagon begins falling freely, and Stark screams at Frieren to not make them suddenly drop. They crash into the ground, but everyone, including the horse, manages to survive the fall without any prominent injuries. Sein uses Goddess's magic to heal the horse, and Frieren apologizes to the merchant for getting them into the situation. However, he tells her not to worry and instead thanks her, as he would have died if he had been traveling alone.

The next day, the group begins repairs on the carriage. As Frieren goes through her luggage, she realizes her ring from Himmel is missing. Meanwhile, Fern, Stark and Sein gather supplies. They talk about the warmer weather, during which Sein notices Fern's bracelet, which Fern reveals is a birthday gift from Stark. Stark laments how it took him three hours to choose. Sein confirms that Stark personally picked out the bracelet and comforts him about how difficult of a situation he must have been in. Stark agrees and complains about how he had to try and read Fern's face for three hours as he picked out her present. Nevertheless, he expresses relief that she ended up happily accepting the gift.

Sein compliments Stark's nature, as he had expected him to be much less charming. With Sein's knowledge about the language of flowers, he reveals to Stark that the mirrored-lotus flower on the bracelet's design means "eternal love," and in this region, such a gift is given by people to their lovers. Fern overhears this and Stark asserts to her that he was not aware of its meaning. He exclaims that he has no knowledge of the language of flowers and that everything was a misunderstanding, causing Fern to bitterly call him an idiot. He points out that Fern was unaware of the meaning too and asks if she would like a different gift instead. Fern rejects the idea, given the amount of effort Stark had put into finding the gift, and she tells him never to bring up such a suggestion again. As Stark apologizes, Sein is amused, and the three of them head back to the camp.

The group camp out over the next few days as they fix the wagon. Every night, Frieren leaves the campsite to search for something, which Fern picks up on. On their last night, Fern follows Frieren. She asks what Frieren is looking for, and the elf mentions the ring that Himmel gave her was missing. Fern offers to aid in the search and tells her that they can delay their departure. Frieren explains that she is used to losing things and Himmel has given her other gifts, so she will give up on searching if she cannot find it that night. Fern points out that if the ring has the same design as her bracelet, it must also mean "eternal love" in the language of flowers. Frieren discloses that she was not aware, and she doubts was Himmel was aware as well. However, Fern expresses that it must be important to her.

After learning about Frieren's missing ring, the merchant says that they should have told him and explains that a few people lost accessories over the years, so he has a spell that finds lost accessories. He mentions that he intended to gift Frieren the spell as a reward for her assistance, and Frieren gladly accepts it. Frieren then flies into the night sky and casts the spell. While doing so, she thinks back to when Himmel rewarded her for her hard work in one of their side quests by letting her pick out something from an accessory stand. She promptly picked out a ring without much thought, and upon seeing her choice, Himmel longingly smiled and thanked the vendor. 

Back in the present, Frieren is able to detect the ring after using the spell, which causes the ring to emit a column of light from within the forest. As she goes to retrieve it, Frieren is reminded of another memory, where she walked alongside Himmel towards the clock tower in the Raad Region's town after they purchased the ring. Himmel called out to Frieren and gave her the ring by kneeling down and sliding it onto her ring finger. The flashback ends with him smiling blissfully as Frieren stands, confused.

With the carriage fixed, the group continues their journey through the forest. Fern mentions that Frieren must be glad to have her lost ring back, and Frieren happily reflects on her memories. She then turns the interest to Fern and asks why she wears a bracelet with a mirrored-lotus motif. This prompts Fern to call Stark an idiot, which causes Stark to mope.

## Episode Notes]

- At the start of the episode, Frieren's Party is shown going through town. While doing so, Frieren recalls the Hero Party's previous visit to the same town, and she looks at a clocktower in the distance. This scene is original to the anime, and it relates to the end of the episode, where Frieren has a memory of Himmel kneeling and sliding the ring with the mirrored-lotus flower motif onto her finger in front of the clocktower.

- In the anime, when Frieren and Sein end their talk on the roof, a scene of Stark gauging Fern's reactions to potential birthday presents follows. In the manga, this scene occurs as a flashback instead in Chapter 31.

- When Frieren explains that flying magic is relatively new to humans, she pictures a demon flying in the air in both the manga and the anime. However, the anime also includes the scenes of Frieren flying to the top of the tower with the blue-moon weed in Episode 3 and Fern carrying Frieren while flying in Episode 4 to illustrate this.

- In the manga, the memory Frieren has when describing Eisen's sturdiness simply depicts the dwarf in an impact crater. The anime extends this scene and includes Eisen diving head first off a cliff and forming the crater upon hitting the ground.

- In the anime, after Frieren kills the aerial monster and the wagon subsequently crash-lands, she states that she considers their plan a success, which evokes comments from Stark and Sein that are not included in the manga.

- In Crunchyroll's English subtitled release of this episode of the anime, the scene in which Himmel gifts Frieren the ring mistakenly has Himmel say that the ring is a reward for Frieren's hard work towards defeating the now-deceased Demon King. This would imply that the scene occurs after the defeat of the Demon King. The original Japanese voice line has no mention of the Demon King, and the English subtitles were later fixed to reflect the correct line. The subtitles now correctly state that Himmel wanted to reward Frieren for a good job on a side quest, which is the same line used in the manga.

## [ARCS] Episode 15
**Smells like Trouble** ｢厄 (やっ) 介 (かい) 事 (ごと) の匂 (にお) い, *Yakkaigoto no nioi*?｣ is the fifteenth episode of the *Frieren: Beyond Journey's End* anime series, released on December 15, 2023.

## Synopsis]

When the party happens upon a town whose inhabitants are all mysteriously asleep, it's time for their newest traveling companion to prove his mettle.

## Plot]

Twenty-nine years after Himmel's passing, Frieren's Party ride a cart through the Laub Hills in the Northern Lands. Frieren reads a book while Fern dozes off. Sein asks how long they have all been traveling together, and Fern tells him she went on the journey with Frieren more than four years ago, with Stark adding in that he has been around for about a year. Sein smiles upon hearing the answers.

Later, Frieren's party continues towards the next village on foot. Sein suddenly remarks that something is missing from their group, which prompts Frieren to list the classes the party currently has. Fern suggests that a thief may be a useful addition, as Frieren always falls for mimic traps. Sein stops and proclaims that most importantly, the party lacks an older woman, and he loudly expresses his belief that every party should have at least one mature lady. Stark points out that Frieren is indeed an older woman, but Sein quickly dismisses the notion. Stark attempts to steer the conversation away from the uncomfortable topic by mentioning that they are approaching the next village.

As they arrive in the village, they are met with a peculiar sight: all the humans appear to be asleep. Fern points out that they are still breathing and Sein confirms this. Stark questions what is going on, and Frieren suggests they leave for the next village to avoid any trouble. Fern chastises Frieren for the suggestion, and Frieren clarifies that she was joking. Sein continues to examine the villagers and deduces that a curse has been cast upon them, which Frieren concurs. Stark asks Frieren for clarification, and she explains that a curse is a spell employed by monsters and demons that could petrify or put people to sleep, and humanity has not yet unraveled them. She adds that they have yet to discover a way to break curses, causing Stark to fear that the village is doomed. Frieren reassures him that there is still hope, as while humanity's magic can not solve it, the Goddesses' magic used by priests is different. She adds that, for a long time, the role of priests is to counter curses.

As Sein works to determine the nature of the curse, the rest of the party enters a building. Stark asks what makes Goddess's magic different from other types of magic, and Frieren explains that the magic is recorded in Holy Scriptures, and only those in possession of these scriptures can use it. Frieren adds that the principles of Goddess's magic are barely understood, much like the magic of demons, and therefore it does not appeal to her. She also notes that the magic is difficult to handle unless one has the "Blessing of The Goddess," which makes one more resistant to curses, giving priests an advantage. Stark asks if even Frieren has a hard time defending against curses, to which she replies that mages cannot detect curses, although she can sense that she is being attacked in some way. Fern voices that she feels anxious, and Stark fearfully wonders if they are being actively cursed.

Sein finishes his examination and proclaims that the curse is rather unique. He suggests that they strike at the source of the curse, otherwise, he would need special equipment, and it would be quicker to deal with the source directly, as he has already determined the location of the monster casting the curse. As soon as they start walking, Stark falls victim to the curse. Frieren asks if Sein can lift the curse temporarily, to which he replies that he can only keep him awake for five seconds. The priest then urges everyone to hurry.

With no other option, they set off towards the monster while carrying Stark with floating magic. Along the way, they make a campfire, and Fern also falls asleep while she rests. Frieren comments that the situation is bad, and Sein and Frieren decide to leave them as they continue looking for the monster. Frieren casts a magical barrier for protection around Fern and Stark, and she and Sein set off towards the monster. When Sein says they are close to it, Frieren tells him to wake her up when the monster appears. As she subsequently starts falling asleep, she warns Sein not to fight the monster alone and that she promises to defeat it. Sein doubts her to do so in the small time he can awaken her. He carries Frieren on his back for the remaining distance between them and the monster, and he says to himself that he also knows offensive magic.

As he arrives at the location of the monster, he sets down Frieren against a tree. As he confronts the flower-like monster, he notes that it is a subspecies of a Chaos Flower, a monster that puts people to sleep and slowly drains their mana, killing them and later using them as fertilizer. Sein thinks about the weak point of all Chaos Flowers and launches a spell—Three Spears of the Goddess—towards the creature's core.

To Sein's surprise, his spell is deflected by the mirror-like leaves of the flower. He realizes that if he cannot strike directly at the core, the creature's leaves will reflect his spells and damage the surrounding areas. He considers waking up Frieren, but he quickly dismisses the idea: as a member of the Hero Party, Frieren's spells are too powerful to risk being deflected and potentially devastate the village they are trying to save. He argues to himself that even if he were to awaken her, they have not yet established mutual understanding with each other and within the five seconds, he does not know if he can communicate where to strike the monster.

However, Sein suddenly recalls a memory of Heiter telling him and his childhood friend about the adventures of the Hero Party. Heiter believes that adventurers like them did not need trust or mutual understanding, as Frieren was terrible at communicating properly. All they needed was to believe in each others' words, and since Frieren proclaimed to defeat the Demon King no matter what, he chose to believe and trust her. Sein recalls Frieren's words to not fight the monster alone and her promise to defeat it, so he decides to believe in her. Using an awakening spell, he manages to rouse Frieren. The mage gets up, and before Sein manages to finish telling her where to aim, she blasts an offensive spell at the weak point of the monster with ease. With the monster dead, Stark wakes up besides a still-asleep Fern, and he wonders what is going on.

Back in the village, the chief, an older woman, thanks Sein. Sein modestly insists that he did not do anything special. The chief gratefully states that the villagers could not have asked for a better way to be reawakened. Sein gleefully smiles as he continues the journey with the rest of the party. Frieren thanks him for his trust and tells him that the moment she woke up, she knew the monster was the type that could reflect spells. Sein calls her incredible, to which she replies that it was thanks to him that they managed to get out alive. She shows her pride in him by patting him on the head. Sein cannot help but think of the beautiful, older villager lady who had thanked him and again bemoans the lack of one in their party.

Frieren's party continues traveling further and reaches the Fortress city of Vorig. The party views the city from a distance, and Frieren starts to explain that Vorig is a relay point to Äußerst, and Fern comments that they are finally halfway there. Frieren suggests they resupply in Vorig, but Fern interrupts her and makes her aware of the party's lack of funds. At that moment, a man calls out to them. He approaches the group from his carriage, accompanied by a servant, and takes a good look at Stark. The nobleman comments on his nice body and that his appearance isn't bad either, prompting him to request they visit him in his mansion. 

Later, the nobleman sits together with Frieren's party in the mansion. The man asks for Stark's name and the boy answers. Frieren calls the man by name, Lord Orden, and tells him that this is the estate of the Orden family, one of the Three Great Knightly Houses of the Northern Lands. Frieren thinks of his grandfather, a previous lord, as a similarly pushy individual, which Orden dismisses as nonsense and expresses that he wants to converse more with Stark. Frieren interrupts again and says Stark is the warrior of their party. The nobleman brushes Frieren off and addresses Stark, telling him he has a request and that he would pay for it. Displeased, Frieren announces that they are leaving. Fern interrupts and shows Frieren their lack of travel funds. Seeing this, Frieren suggests that they hear what Lord Orden has to say.

Lord Orden asks about Stark's hometown, and Stark tells him he is from a village in the Klee Region in the Central Lands. Orden mentions that his family line also originated from that village. They gather in front of a large portrait, and Orden explains that it shows his eldest son, Wirt. Fern comments that Stark and him look alike, and Orden agrees. Frieren asks what this has to do with Orden's request. The nobleman explains that a month before, they fought a large battle against demons, and Wirt sacrificed himself to take down the enemy's general. He recalls the memory of his last moments with Wirt, and he reveals to Frieren's party that only his butler, Gabel, and some of their nearest confidants are aware of Wirt's death. 

Frieren asks how Stark would fit into the picture. Orden explains that Vorig is the key to the region's defense and he cannot allow morale to fall. There will be a social gathering of influential figures within the region in three months, and Stark would show up as Wirt's replacement. Frieren asks what the pay would be, and Orden offers ten Strahl gold coins. Fern whispers to the elf that this payment is enough for three meals a day and snacks for a year. Frieren wants a grimoire added to their reward, and Orden accepts the extra condition. Stark presents his scar on the face as a problem, but Orden is of the opinion that the people think Wirt is currently in recovery, and a battle scar would be something honorable. Fern then reaffirms that they need the money and Stark, in low spirits, agrees. After reaching an agreement, Orden orders Gabel to teach Stark proper etiquette.

Two of the three months until the event pass as Stark studies etiquette. He is trained on how to ride horses and dance, and he receives general education. Meanwhile, the other members enjoy their free time. Fern meets Stark in one of the estate's hallways and tells him his training appears to be taking a toll on him. When she about his progress, the young man kneels, takes her hand, looks up at her, and asks in return what she thinks. Fern replies that his behavior does not suit him. Stark then stands up and wanders off, leaving Fern alone, and she looks at the hand he had taken.

Lord Orden stands in thought in front of the portrait of Wirt, and Stark meets him, addressing him as "Lord Orden." The nobleman reminds him to say "father" in his presence, as there could always be somebody watching. Stark tells him that he thinks this is too cold considering how recently his son passed, but Orden says that it would have been his son's final wish. Orden admits to not enjoying the plan either but requests for Stark's cooperation. Stark and Orden walk outside into the backyard, where they come across a young boy who is practicing with a sword. Orden introduces him to Stark as his second son, Mut. Orden gives the child strict advice and says to Stark that his heir shows little improvement. Stark immediately recalls memories of his past about his father in the presence of Stoltz, regarding him as a failure.

While the nobleman gives Stark training in the family's technique, Stark asks what Orden thinks of his young son. Orden describes Mut as someone who may not have as much talent as brother, but as he works hard over time, he will grow to someone that could surpass himself. Stark feels relieved and tells him he should explicitly communicate this to his son as encouragement for the boy. Orden states that he already has, but it has seemingly gone to his head and Mut lacks improvement as a result. Stark playfully acknowledges that this is a problem.

Later, Frieren, Fern, and Lord Orden meet at tea time, where Orden reveals that Fern should also learn etiquette, shocking her. Orden points out that the event is a social gathering and asks if a young man is expected to attend it alone. He asks Frieren if she would prefer to escort him instead like a mother, but Frieren passes the duty off to Fern, wishing her good luck. Fern subsequently goes through the same training by the female staff in etiquette and dance while Sein and Frieren continue enjoying leisurely activities. 

Another month passes, and the evening of the social gathering begins. The ballroom comprises of various noble figures, alongside Frieren's party and Lord Orden. Fern sits in a dress while Stark stands beside her in uniform. The young woman comments that the past month was hellish, and Stark reminds her of her own words that they needed the money. Stark kneels, takes Fern's hand, and requests a dance, as they had practiced for it anyway. She tells him once again that this behavior does not suit him, but she reluctantly follows him to the dance floor. Alongside the other pairs in the ballroom, they dance to music while executing their choreography. They soon get into the dance and appear to enjoy the ambience, and Lord Orden and other guests watch them and appear to be taken in. Frieren sits at a table accompanied by Sein. He asks the elf if she would like to dance too, but Frieren focuses on eating cake and refuses.

Lord Orden takes a break in an empty side room and is accompanied by Gabel. He blames his eye injury for not being in the front lines, which may have changed Wirt's fate. As the butler tries to cheer him up, Stark arrives, and Orden confirms that the ball is coming to an end, which means Stark has fulfilled his duty. The Lord commands Gabel to reward Frieren and sends him out. Orden compliments Stark for being a powerful warrior and implies that he could stay here, but the young man declines the offer, as he is not a replacement for his son. The nobleman agrees and says he cannot be a replacement for Stark's father, either. Disappointed, Orden then reveals that he had an argument with Wirt and said something he didn't mean, leading him to part with Wirt in anger right before his death, and he recalls the day in his memory. He expresses his belief that him finding Stark was a miracle. However, for Stark, who recalls Eisen's face, explains that this is just one more reason he cannot stay, as he also said something he didn't mean with the man that raised him, and he wants to bring him stories of his travels. Reinvigorated, Lord Orden accepts the decision.

After the social gathering concludes, Frieren spends half a day looking through grimoires, struggling to choose one. An exhausted Gabel watches over her, and Fern urges Frieren to pick one and not distress the butler even further. Meanwhile, Stark stands with Sein near a window and watches the backyard. Sein remarks that it will take time before the city can rebuild the forces. Stark, however, is just pleased to see Orden training together with Mut, and he comments that Orden does not have to worry about his heir at least.
